Zhejiang Public Association Appeals for Gradual Collection of Overdue Taxes 87

Yesterday, a touching plea was submitted to the Zhejiang Provincial Government.

The Zhejiang Public Association in this port submitted a document to Huang, Chairman of the Zhejiang Provincial Government, and Cheng, Director of the Finance Department: "The people owe old taxes because of years of famine and excessive surcharges, making it impossible to pay on time. This is not intentional tax evasion. During the first phase of tax collection, tax collectors and officials abused their authority and used coercion, causing further disturbances. For minor overdue amounts, people were summoned and detained. Those who complied with the summons and paid were still suddenly arrested. Ancestral temples and public property were ordered to be liquidated to cover the taxes of one person. People with similar surnames were mistakenly detained. Relatives and even cohabitants were implicated and arrested. Detentions even extended to women and children, filling the prisons. All of this is factual. Fellow villagers from various places have repeatedly come to the association to complain and request a petition.

Hoping for Leniency

We have repeatedly declined, not daring to submit the petition, because tax revenue is the province's legitimate income and paying taxes is the people's duty. Although the collection procedures may have been too strict, the years of arrears are ultimately the people's own fault. Now that the first phase has ended, we hear that the amount collected is not too small. At a time when the people's resources are scarce, taking flesh to heal wounds causes deep pain. We dare not use the analogy of Mount Tai, a fierce tiger, or Liu Zongyuan's snake catcher to compare ourselves, but the people are exhausted and deserve a short respite. If a little more time is granted, it would be a great favor from a benevolent person. Furthermore, taxes have been in arrears for as long as nine years, and it is impossible to recover them all in one year. The people's resources are limited and blood will eventually run dry. Our association humbly

Submits a Plea on Behalf of the People

We propose that the continued collection of old taxes, scheduled for September of this year, be postponed until April or May of next year so that indebted households can prepare in advance and avoid a last-minute scramble. This would also prevent the new taxes from being affected. We also request that the deadline for settlement be extended and that a system of phased repayment be implemented, allowing households with larger arrears to pay in installments. This would alleviate the people's suffering and facilitate financial planning, benefiting both sides. We urgently submit this petition, hoping that your government will investigate, approve, and implement it. We would be deeply grateful. The Shanghai Zhejiang Public Association respectfully salutes."

Lottery Drawing for Three Types of National Bonds for Reconstructing War Zones Held Yesterday 88

A Total of Fifteen Winning Tickets were Drawn for a Total of 3.2 Million Yuan in Principal Repayment

Principal Repayment for Unified War Zone Bonds to be Paid at the End of July; Principal Repayment for Reconstruction Bonds to be Paid at the End of August.

The lottery drawing for the first principal repayment of the Type E unified national bonds for 1936, the first principal repayment of the reconstruction bonds for 1936, and the eleventh principal repayment of the short-term national bonds for relieving war zones in North China for 1933 was held at the Bankers' Association yesterday at 10 a.m. Those in attendance included: Tao Changshan, Director of the National Bonds Department; Lin Jinyu, supervisor from the Auditing Department; Xu Jilong from the Municipal Chamber of Commerce; Fan Jietang from the National Debt Fund Association; Li Shijun from the Hebei Provincial Government; Zhuang Dezhi from the Bankers' Association; Yan Dayou from the Money Trade Association; Wang Xiangshu from the North China War Zone Short-Term National Bond Fund Association; and lottery drawers Jin Wenyuan from the Central Bank, Zhu Qizhen from the Bank of China, and Chen Xun from the Bank of Communications, and over thirty other people. The meeting was presided over by Tao Changshan, Director of the National Bonds Department.

Chairman's Report

Chairman Tao Changshan reported: "Today is the lottery drawing for the first principal repayment of the Type E unified national bonds for 1936, the first principal repayment of the reconstruction bonds for 1936, and the eleventh principal repayment of the short-term national bonds for relieving war zones in North China for 1933. The lottery method is as follows: for the Type E unified national bonds and the reconstruction bonds, the last three digits of the bond number will be used; for the war zone bonds, the last two digits will be used. Now, I will briefly report on the details of each type of bond:

The Type E unified national bonds for 1936 were issued in February 1936, with a fixed amount of 260 million yuan in national currency. This is the first principal repayment, with five winning tickets drawn, each worth 260,000 yuan, for a total principal repayment of 1.3 million yuan.

The reconstruction bonds for 1936 were issued in March 1936, with a fixed amount of 340 million yuan in national currency. This is the first principal repayment, with five winning tickets drawn, each worth 340,000 yuan, for a total principal repayment of 1.7 million yuan.

The short-term national bonds for relieving war zones in North China for 1933 were issued in November 1933, with a fixed amount of 4 million yuan in national currency. The first through tenth principal repayments have already been drawn. This is the eleventh principal repayment, with five winning tickets drawn: two tickets will be drawn from the first to fourth sets of tickets, each worth 46,000 yuan; and three tickets will be drawn from the fifth to tenth sets of tickets, each worth 36,000 yuan, for a total principal repayment of 200,000 yuan. The principal and accrued interest of the above-mentioned winning bonds will be paid starting on July 31st for the Type E unified national bonds and the war zone bonds, and starting on August 31st for the reconstruction bonds. The war zone bonds will continue to be paid by the Central Bank, the Bank of China, and the Bank of Communications in Peiping and Tianjin. The Type E unified national bonds and the reconstruction bonds will be paid by the Central Bank in various locations and by the Bank of China, the Bank of Communications, and the Central Trust Bureau entrusted by the Central Bank. Furthermore, to facilitate bondholders and expedite payment, holders of the Type E unified national bonds and the reconstruction bonds may discount the bond certificates and the coupons expiring at the end of July for the Type E unified national bonds and the coupons expiring at the end of August for the reconstruction bonds at the Bank of China and the Bank of Communications, and may rediscount them at the Central Bank. The Ministry of Finance has notified the three banks to proceed accordingly on February 15, 1936. That concludes my report. Now, I would like to ask the supervisors to verify the drawing tickets and the drawing ticket ledgers so that we can proceed with the lottery drawing."

Winning Numbers

After the Chairman's report was completed and the supervisors verified the drawing tickets and the drawing ticket ledgers, the lottery drawing began. The winning numbers are listed below:

The five winning numbers for the Type E unified national bonds for 1936 are: 079, 272, 382, 408, and 880.

The five winning numbers for the reconstruction bonds for 1936 are: 139, 292, 452, 760, and 824.

The five winning numbers for the short-term national bonds for relieving war zones in North China for 1933 are: 16, 26, 46, 71, and 99. The meeting adjourned at 11 a.m.

Ancient Artifacts in Storage: Centuries-Old Paintings and Calligraphy Exposed to the Sun 89

Staff Members Bravely Conduct Inventory Under the Scorching Heat

The ancient artifacts from the Peiping Palace Museum that were moved to Shanghai for safekeeping have been undergoing inventory and inspection since Shu Chushi was appointed by the Ministry of Education to supervise the process two years ago. Due to the heavy workload, progress has been slow, and the entire process is still not complete after nearly two years. Currently, all types of utensils, bronzes, and paintings and calligraphy from the previous dynasties and the Tang and Song dynasties have been unpacked and inspected. The Yuan, Ming, and Qing dynasty artifacts are particularly numerous and of high quality, accounting for seventy to eighty percent of the collection and being in better condition than those preserved from previous dynasties. In this humid and hot season, the Shanghai office, following the instructions of Museum Director Ma Heng, has been working harder to complete the task as soon as possible. Therefore, Section Chief Ouyang Banghua, along with supervising committee member Shu Chushi, have been bravely continuing the inventory in the storage rooms on Tianzhu Church Street, working diligently under the scorching heat. In addition to the inventory work, it has been discovered that a large number of embroidery and paintings and calligraphy have mildew spots during this humid season. Section Chief Ouyang personally supervised the staff in opening the boxes and taking out the items one by one to expose them to the sun, in order to preserve them in good condition.

Resolution of the Yangtze River Piece Goods Merchant Guild's Strike 90

Two Million Worth of Stockpiled Goods Have Begun Loading

Water Freight Modification is Under Discussion

On the first of this month, the six companies of the Yangtze River shipping lines announced the implementation of a measuring system for piece goods and Western cloth going upstream, and also an increase in water freight to 13.6 yuan per ton (40 chi). The piece goods merchant guild in Shanghai and various customs brokers along the Yangtze River repeatedly negotiated with the six companies, but failed to achieve the goal of reducing freight costs. Therefore, starting from July 1st, they implemented a final measure against the six shipping companies for all piece goods and Western cloth being shipped to the Yangtze River:

A Unified Strike

On one hand, the piece goods industry publicly elected Chen Panjun, a leader of the customs brokers' association, to negotiate with the six companies, aiming to achieve a more lenient allowance for measurements (according to the new regulations, each piece was only allowed 18 chi, a difference of 12 chi from the original box size) and to reduce freight costs. Because water freight charged according to the new regulations resulted in a difference of as much as 4.7 yuan per box of piece goods, negotiations lasting more than ten days had not yet yielded a definite solution, leading to a stockpile of four to five thousand pieces of Yangtze River piece goods in Shanghai, worth two million yuan. Finally, because both sides were resolute, which was not beneficial to either "commerce" or "shipping," Wu Delin, the deputy manager of the Sanbei Company, stepped in to

Reconcile with Merchants

Using peaceful methods for mediation, he also consulted with the authorities of various shipping companies such as Taikoo, Nissin, Ewo, and China Merchants, to provide piece goods merchants with a way out, to prevent the strike from lasting too long or expanding, and to avoid unnecessary sacrifices for both sides. At the same time, he requested Chen Panjun to contact the merchants and ensure that the strike was ended and loading resumed as soon as possible. It was decided that the increase in fees and the measuring system would be

Postponed for Half a Month

To be implemented on July 15th. At the same time, the six companies agreed to accommodate the opinions put forward by Chen Panjun and others, and to reduce the new water freight rates. However, the large quantities of piece goods already piled up in various warehouses had to be shipped first, and would still be given preferential treatment with the original water freight rates, with as many Chinese ships being used as possible. The commercial shipping to Hunan Province, which had been interrupted due to previous incidents, had now come to an end, and telegrams were being sent to Shanghai urging the shipment of goods. The piece goods merchants, following Wu's proposal, had accepted the mediation plan and called off the strike starting from the 9th, and since the beginning of this week, they had already

Started Reporting Shipments

Up to today, at least two to three thousand boxes of piece goods and Western cloth have been loaded, of which five-tenths are destined for Hunan Province, and the rest to Jiujiang and Hankou. Taikoo and Sanbei, among others, have therefore opened direct routes to Hunan to expedite the upstream transport of piece goods. The China Merchants Bureau has also decided to dispatch the Jiangjing ship to Changsha to transport these goods. As for the modification of the newly set water freight rates, the six companies will convene another meeting to decide on it, and then notify the merchants. It is expected that a decision can be reached around the 15th. A major strike by the Yangtze River piece goods merchants has come to an end.

South Seas Commercial Inspection Group to Depart on the 16th 94

Group Leader Gao Shiheng, Deputy Leader Hu Shicheng, Secretary Yang Chong, and Twelve Group Members

The China Industrial and Foreign Trade Association, in view of the fact that our country's industry has been backward in recent years, imports have increased sharply, commerce has declined, rural areas have gone bankrupt, and domestic goods industries have also felt the difficulty of finding a way out and have no room for development, specially organized the South Seas Commercial Inspection Group. Inspection Tasks: The group will hold national goods sample exhibitions in the above-mentioned locations, establish permanent national goods display halls, proclaim the latest status of the national goods industry in the motherland, the manufacturing situation of various factories, investigate the living conditions of overseas Chinese in the South Seas, study and improve the goods they commonly use to suit their psychology and preferences, investigate the trends of the South Seas market and the level of general purchasing power, investigate the currency and exchange situation in the South Seas, investigate the taxes and fees in the South Seas, seek standards and transportation procedures, contact the South Seas business community to negotiate methods for distributing national goods, contact overseas Chinese in the South Seas, introduce national goods, and agree to communicate with the industrial and commercial sectors of the motherland at any time, contact local government agencies, consulates, chambers of commerce, and patriotic overseas Chinese who are engaged in the national goods movement.

There are also overseas Chinese from various places in the South Seas who, due to time and economic constraints, cannot attend, but have sent letters and telegrams requesting a stopover and have also prepared a welcome. This shows the eagerness of overseas Chinese for the motherland's industrial and commercial development abroad, and their enthusiasm to purchase national goods.

Around the World Grand Tour by Air 95

American Dr. Falconner Arrives in Shanghai

The Mainland News reported that Dr. Falconner of the United States, embracing the ambitious goal of flying around the world in seventeen days, arrived in Shanghai on Thursday. Mr. Falconner departed from his hometown in Texas and flew to Lakehurst, New Jersey, where he transferred to the Hindenburg airship and headed east, crossing the Atlantic Ocean and arriving in Frankfurt, Germany. He then flew to Amsterdam and caught a KLM Royal Dutch Airlines flight to Penang, marking the tenth day since his departure from his hometown. However, his travel speed has slowed down slightly because Pan American's Pacific aviation business has not yet extended to Macau. Therefore, he came to Shanghai on the President Jackson, and may wait until Pacific aviation extends to Macau in September before continuing his journey. According to Mr. Falconner's estimate, it will take a week to fly from Macau to his hometown, so he can complete the feat of flying around the world in two and a half weeks. In the future, he may rent a plane from Hong Kong to fly to Macau, so that not a single foot of the 30,000-mile journey will be on the ground. Mr. Falconner booked a through ticket with the American Express Company at a cost of US$3,305, of which the Hindenburg cost US$400. As far as safety is concerned, the Graf Zeppelin airship has flown to South America 104 times, carrying 30,000 passengers, without any accidents. In the future, when the various routes are connected, flying around the world will become a common occurrence. Mr. Falconner had previously traveled around the world four times, and this time he is doing it out of curiosity, planning to write about his experiences for North American newspapers. Because he is passing through in a hurry, he cannot observe everything in detail, but he will stay for a few days in interesting places along the way. He left his hometown on May 8th and arrived in Penang on May 28th, spending a few days in New York in between. After arriving in Hong Kong, he stayed for a week and will stay for some time in China and Japan. Mr. Falconner graduated from Harvard Medical School and previously served as a civil affairs official in the American government, stationed in Manila for several years.

French Concession to Collect Police Tax on Vacant Houses 96

Because They Need to be Taken Care of by the Police and Fire Department

The Shanghai Times reported that the French Concession's Board of Directors passed a new regulation on June 22 stipulating that a portion of the police tax will be levied on all shops and apartments that have been built but are unoccupied. This has led to rumors that all vacant houses will be subject to the police tax. However, an official from the Board of Directors denied this yesterday, saying that according to the new regulations, shops that have been built but are unoccupied will be charged 50% of the Concession police tax, which is 65% of the rent. Apartments that have been built but are unoccupied will be charged 75%, which is 97.5% of the rent. Landlords who want to charge high rents or rent out quickly will be willing to pay this tax. The implementation of the new regulations is because all built houses need to be taken care of by the police and fire department. As for houses that are vacant due to residents being away, no tax will be collected.

The Executive Yuan Cables Order to Halt Issuance of Yellow River Disaster Relief and Charity Lottery Tickets 97

And Sends Telegrams to all Provinces and Cities Forbidding Sales

The Shanghai Municipal Government, based on a report from the Social Affairs Bureau, stated that the Yellow River flood relief lottery is being continuously issued, and the Tianjin Public Welfare Charity Lottery is also being promoted in the market. Whether these two lottery tickets have been approved and whether they should be banned was specifically inquired of the Ministry of Finance for verification and reply. In addition to submitting a request to the Executive Yuan a few days ago, cabling an order to the Hebei-Chahar Political Council to instruct a halt, the Executive Yuan also requested that the Yuan send telegrams to the provincial and municipal governments, ordering them to strictly prohibit sales in order to avoid hindering the promotion of aviation highway construction lottery tickets.

Thirteen Silk Factories in the Xinzha District Completely Strike 98

Because the Factories Refused to Restore Original Wages, the Social Affairs Bureau Called Both Parties for Mediation Yesterday Without Results

— Factories in the Hongkou and Southern Shanghai Districts Shifted to Half-Day Work Yesterday —

The Dagong She reported that the silk workers in thirteen silk factories along Guangfu Road in the Xinzha District of this city, due to the factories' refusal to restore original wages, declared a joint strike starting on the 7th of this month. The Social Affairs Bureau specially summoned both labor and management to the bureau yesterday afternoon for mediation. Other silk factories in the Hongkou and Zhabei Nanshi districts of the Concession, a total of thirty factories, have switched to half-day work due to the hot weather. The Dagong She reporter has investigated and recorded the details below.

Joint Strike of Silk Factories in Xinzha

The silk factories in Xinzhabei that are operating include Da Feng and Cheng Feng (Guangfu Road), Hong Tai and Xie Xing and Yi Chang (Hengfeng Road), Tai Lun and Fu Chang II factories (Chang'an Road), Ji Yu and Jiu Yu (Gonghe Road) and other thirteen silk factories, employing approximately 16,000 female workers. The silk factory wages in this city before the January 28th Incident were 6 jiao per day, but were changed to 5 jiao 1 fen after the January 28th Incident. The wage was reduced to 3 jiao 8 fen in the year before last. Last year, due to a slight improvement in the silk market, the wage was increased to 4 jiao per day. After the factories in this district started work this year, the silk workers demanded the restoration of 5 jiao 5 fen per day, but the factories could not afford it, resulting in no resolution. After the meal break in the afternoon of the 7th of this month, the female workers of the Tai Lun silk factory in Chang'an Road first refused to enter the factory to work, resulting in a strike. This then spread to Xie Xing silk factory and Hong Tai silk factory and neighboring silk factories. Fearing the strike, workers came to cause trouble, so they unanimously released the workers who were working, and they did not resume work on the morning of the 8th, holding out until yesterday, which was the third day, and they still had not resumed work.

The Labor Union Announces the Strike Process

The Dagong She reporter interviewed the person in charge of the Sixth District Silk Workers Union yesterday and spoke about the fact that silk workers' organizations in this city have been extremely scattered in the past, and management has also been difficult because of their low level of education. In order to achieve sound organization and facilitate training, the union has applied to the party and government agencies to handle worker registration. However, this work can only be completed with the cooperation of labor and management, but a small number of management personnel do not understand the truth and have expressed suspicion, so the work has not been carried out. Regarding this labor dispute, although the workers are demanding the restoration of wages, the organizational aspect also has a considerable impact, so it is hoped that the labor dispute will be resolved as soon as possible, and the factories should support the union in carrying out worker registration, so that labor disputes can be reduced in the future. Furthermore, after the union's persuasion, the silk factories in other areas have understood the truth, so there will be no more labor disputes.

The Authorities' Mediation Yields No Results

In order to prevent the expansion of the labor dispute, the political and government authorities specially summoned both labor and management to the bureau at 2 PM yesterday for mediation by the Social Affairs Bureau. Yuan Yunlong and Yang Gengti of the Sixth District Silk Workers Union, Shen Huachen and Zhang Peishen of the Trade Association, and Zhu Yangwu representing the Municipal Party Department attended. After inquiring about the situation, Zhu Guilin, chairman of the Mediation Section of the Social Affairs Bureau, proposed that labor restore 5 jiao 1 fen per day, and management only agreed to add 4 fen per day, which is 4 jiao 4 fen, and shorten the working hours by one hour. Because the two sides' opinions did not come close, there was no result. The Social Affairs Bureau has scheduled another mediation for 9 AM on Tuesday. On the workers' side, the strike will continue.

Other Factories Shift to Half-Day Work

Recently, due to the hot weather and the sluggishness of the overseas silk market, ten factories in the Hongkou District, such as Xingchangxiang and Chengfuren, three factories in the Concession District, such as Ewo, Xin Chang, and Tong Yu, seventeen factories in the Zhabei District, such as Yu Feng, Xing Lun, Hengtai Zhicheng, Yu Feng, and two factories in the Nanshi District, such as Guangyuan and Baotai, a total of thirty-two silk factories, have reduced working hours to half-day work starting yesterday. The working hours are from 5 AM to 12 PM, and all work is stopped and rested in the afternoon. Once the weather cools down, full-day shifts will resume.

After Heated Debate by Lawyers for Both Sides, the Japanese Sailor Case Concludes Yesterday; Prosecutor Zhang Chongru's Opinion on the Case; Ye Haisheng and Others Lack Sufficient Criminal Suspicion; Court Schedules Sentencing for Next Friday Morning 109

Yesterday at 2 PM, the First Special District Court continued to investigate the case of Japanese sailor Nakayama Hideo, who died from a gunshot wound by a sniper. Judge Qian Hongye, along with Judges Xiao Xiefen and Feng Shide, and Prosecutor Zhang Chongru, and Clerk Ding Chongnan, ascended to the first criminal court. After ordering the defendants Yang Wendao, Ye Haisheng, and Zhou Sherong to be brought forward, Lawyer Ru Bao, representing the police station in the prosecution, immediately stated that there was still a witness, a Portuguese man, who last year on the night of November 9th, in Room 4 of the Yuegong Hotel, witnessed Ye Haisheng returning from committing the crime and talking with a guest in Room 9. This witness had already been summoned and could testify about Ye's demeanor at the time of the conversation. The court then ordered the Portuguese man to the witness stand and questioned him. According to the translated testimony, he worked for the Salvation Society and that night went to Room 4 of the Yuegong Hotel to visit a Cantonese friend, Li Tian. He then saw the door of Room 9 half-open, with Ye Haisheng's foot across the threshold, his face pale. The guest in Room 9, Lin Renxiao, asked him why he looked like that. Ye replied that he had just returned from a fight outside. The Portuguese man also testified that he knew Yang Wendao from the Guangdong Club in Guangzhou several years ago, and he knew Zhou Sherong there as well, but only for a short time. He knew Ye Haisheng from the

dance hall. The court questioned the three defendants, Yang, and the others, all of whom admitted to knowing the Portuguese man. Zhou even stated that when he was arrested at the Mainland Dance Hall this time, the man identified himself as a detective. Ye Haisheng then claimed that although he knew the man, he had been beaten up, and that his statements were purely fictional. At this point in the questioning, all the witnesses had testified. The lawyers for both sides then began their verbal arguments, unleashing their eloquent tongues. First, the prosecuting lawyer, Ru Bao, detailed the entire case from beginning to end, and based on various pieces of evidence and testimonies, asserted that the defendants should bear joint

responsibility for murder. He presented his reasons in detail for over an hour and fifteen minutes. He stated that after the court's thorough investigation, what needed attention was the various pieces of evidence to determine if the defendants were involved in the murder. The fact that Nakayama Hideo died from a gunshot wound was undisputed. After the incident, no fewer than one or two hundred police officers from the police station and Japanese military command investigated the scene, and many onlookers gathered. After two hours of investigation, a handgun bullet and shell casing were found and taken back to the police station for inspection (it was determined that this was the murder weapon. The investigation of the murderer then began. At the time, a woman, now

departed from Shanghai, Pu Qiaoying, and Hu Xianghe, who had previously been summoned to testify, happened to pass the scene and witnessed the two murderers fleeing. Based on their descriptions and other information, the defendants were arrested. Furthermore, because Ye Haisheng confessed that the handgun was given to him by Yang Wendao, Yang's home was searched, and the book in which the handgun was hidden was found. Later, Yang claimed that the book had been framed, which led to questions of a swap and false accusation. However, after thorough investigation and the testimony of various witnesses proving that Yang Wendao admitted to the situation when the book was found and brought back to the police station, it was clear that the physics book belonged to Yang and there was no doubt. Yang tried to deny everything, and cunningly claimed that the

book in which he hid the handgun was a different book, and that the handgun was also different. However, when the police station retrieved the handgun with the serial number provided by Yang and placed it in the hole in this book, it did not fit at all. This showed that the hole in this book could only hold the murder weapon. His claim of being framed was not credible. If the hole in the book was dug by someone else, how could it fit this gun so perfectly? Furthermore, the gun had only been taken by the Japanese military command for nine days since it was found, and the rest of the time it was in the custody of the police station. There was no way for others to have the opportunity to copy it exactly. Moreover, the rust on the gun matched the rust on the book in over forty-two points. There was no

opportunity for forgery, and there were so many similarities, how could he deny it? In conclusion, this gun was the murder weapon, and the book in which the gun was hidden was found in Yang's home. Although Yang denied that the book was his original book, claiming that Yang Jianzhong had framed him, and repeatedly claimed ignorance about the case, without other strong evidence to the contrary, he could not escape his guilt. As for Ye Haisheng, when he was arrested in Qingdao, he did not know that Yang had already been arrested and the murder weapon had been found, so he still tried to deny it. Later, when he learned that the evidence was irrefutable and there was no room for denial, he confessed without hesitation during the third interrogation. Afterwards, with each

interrogation, his confession became clearer. He was not an ignorant person, and knew the seriousness of the crime of murder. If he was not involved, why would he risk admitting to it? However, during the interrogation on May 27th, he suddenly recanted his confession, claiming that his previous confessions were due to torture by the police station. When the defendant's lawyer visited Ye at the police station on May 21st, Ye told his lawyer that the police station treated him very well and did not mention being tortured. Moreover, when the judge inspected the scene of the incident on May 20th, if Ye had been wronged, he could have refused to reenact the crime, as the police station would not have tortured him at that time. However, he calmly reenacted the scene of the crime from beginning to end, and even corrected the testimony of witness Hu Xianghe regarding Ye's escape

route after the shooting. This proved that the reenactment was voluntary and must have matched the facts. Unexpectedly, he acted the way he did on the 27th, and cried in court about the types of torture he had suffered, claiming that one was burning his lips with cigarettes, and another was pouring tap water into his nose. Because he could not bear the torture, he secretly swallowed a copper key he had hidden on his person to commit suicide. However, the police station conducted thorough searches of the suspects, ensuring that they had nothing on them. Later, Ye was sent to a mountain hospital, where an X-ray showed that there was no metal in his stomach. Ye then claimed that what he swallowed must have been excreted. The slight injuries on his lips were also examined and proven not to be burns. Even if the police station had

used torture, it must have been used on those who were trying to evade the law. If Ye had already confessed repeatedly, there was no need to torture him. If it was believed that torture would force Ye to make a false confession, then why not torture Yang and Zhou as well? Although Ye presented evidence to the contrary, he could only prove his whereabouts on November 8th and 10th, but not on the 9th when the incident occurred. As for Zhou Sherong, Ye confessed that he had participated in the conspiracy, making him an accomplice. He should be sentenced to death for murder. Then, Lawyer Ge Zhaoji defended Yang Wendao and Zhou Sherong, saying that Yang Wendao originally had a

book in which he hid a handgun, and that Yang Jianzhong taught him how to dig the hole in 1934. Because there were many children in the defendant's family, hiding it this way would avoid danger. The book suddenly disappeared in February of this year, and he only saw it again on the day it was found. Therefore, the defendant suspected that Yang Jianzhong had swapped this book for the original book to frame him. Zhou Sherong had nothing to do with the case and should be declared innocent. Lawyer Guo Qiming also defended Yang once more. Ye Haisheng's appointed lawyers, Zhang Zhirang and Fan Gang, then spoke. Lawyer Zhang used the forensic institute's report as the focus of his defense, asserting that the three defendants

were not involved. The person who killed Nakayama Hideo was a third party. The main point was that the report stated that the deceased's injury was caused by someone very close to him, so the shooter must have been walking shoulder to shoulder with the deceased and could not have been Ye. The investigation showed that on the day the deceased was attacked, he went to four brothels from morning to night. This showed that he was quite amorous and welcomed by the prostitutes. He left the brothel at 8:40 PM and was shot on the way. It was clear that his death was due to a love rivalry. The fact that Ye and others were implicated was purely the result of

people trying to obtain a reward, a fabricated act. Yang Wendao did not examine the book carefully at first and assumed that it was his original book. Under pressure, he mistook a deer for a horse. Yang Jianzhong was Wendao's nephew, and he was willing to report his uncle's address to those who wanted to get to his uncle. Why would he hesitate to swap the book? The locations where the bullet and shell casing were found were not where the sailor fell, and it was difficult to prove that the bullet had been stained with blood. Therefore, it could not be determined that the sailor's injury was caused by this gun and bullet. Furthermore, what was found in Yang's home was not a handgun, but only a book for hiding a gun. Therefore, Yang was not suspected of any crime. Ye Haisheng had

nothing to do with the gun and bullets. Although he confessed to being the murderer, there were many contradictions between his confession and the facts of the case, so it was difficult to believe. He should be acquitted. Then, Lawyer Fan and Lawyer Tang Huaiqun and Lawyer Wang Shizong, representing Zhou Sherong, finished their arguments. Prosecutor Zhang then gave his opinion, stating that Yang Wendao initially admitted that the book was his, but later claimed that Yang Jianzhong had secretly swapped it. Considering the relationship between the two, Jianzhong certainly had the possibility of making the swap. The results of the forensic examination also determined that the book

appeared to be forged. Therefore, the evidence of Wendao's crime was weak and insufficient. Although Ye Haisheng had confessed, his reenactment was often contrary to the facts. Furthermore, in the days before and after Nakayama Hideo's death, Ye's behavior was normal and showed no abnormalities. From this perspective, the suspicion of crime was also insufficient. Zhou Sherong was even less involved. He should be judged according to the law. Judge Qian then scheduled sentencing for next Friday (the 17th) morning. Yang and the others were returned to custody, and the court adjourned at 6 PM.

Shanghai Port Contagious Disease Report by the Harbour Quarantine Office 110

Last Week, No Cholera Found in the Port, Dysentery and Typhoid Fever Patients Most Numerous

The Shanghai Harbour General Quarantine Office yesterday issued a report on the contagious disease situation in Shanghai Port for the week ending midnight on the 4th of this month. Typhoid fever and dysentery were the most numerous types of illness. No virulent contagious diseases such as plague and cholera were found. The types of illness and the number of patients and deaths are recorded below. Last week in Shanghai Port, there were two Chinese smallpox patients and one foreign patient. One Chinese person died. There were two Chinese patients with epidemic cerebrospinal meningitis and one death. There were twenty Chinese patients with typhoid fever and one foreign patient. Sixteen Chinese people died. There were twelve Chinese patients with bacterial dysentery and amoebic dysentery and one foreign patient. Three Chinese people died. There were five Chinese diphtheria patients and one foreign patient. Two Chinese people died. There were six Chinese patients with scarlet fever and three foreign patients. One foreign person died. In total, forty-seven Chinese people contracted contagious diseases and eight foreigners. Twenty-three Chinese people died and one foreigner.

Shantytown Residents in the Eastern District Complain 111

Yesterday Due to the Municipal Council's Order to Demolish, They Requested the Municipal Federation to Uphold Justice

Due to the Municipal Council's limited order to demolish shantytowns in the Eastern District, representatives Sun Hankui, Wang Qitai, Yang Jingchen, Guo Zhizhi, Gu Xuebo, Jia Zidong, Tang Anping, Jiang Shanchang, Zhang Buyun, Xu Yangguang, Ji Yunsheng, Yin Yifu, Liu Xuede, Wang Ruyu, Sun Xuzhou, Wang Daomeng, and over ten others, went to the First Special District Municipal Federation in the afternoon at 2 PM to petition. Secretary Zhao Ziyun of the Federation received them. Their petition stated: "To the gentlemen of the Shanghai Municipal Federation, we, the shantytown residents of the East Shanghai District, number approximately five thousand households or more. Recently, the Municipal Council came to inspect our shantytowns and ordered us to move out voluntarily within one month, otherwise they will forcibly demolish them. We, more than five thousand shantytown households, are extremely terrified by this news. We are not resisting the Municipal Council's order, but we are truly in unbearable pain. Because the market is sluggish, the economy is shrinking, industry is withering, and the countryside is bankrupt, all industries are in decline. No one can deny that Chinese industry has stopped, closed down, and is being realized simultaneously. The wages in Japanese cotton mills are low, and the construction industry is also hanging up signs that they are not starting work. Even the Municipal Council, in order to provide temporary work, has dismissed permanent workers and established five-day shifts. Nine out of ten homes are empty. We shantytown residents have also reached a critical juncture. Because young and strong people work only half a month, earning an average of four jiao per day, and rely on six yuan per month. If it is just one person, they can barely survive. Otherwise, which family does not have elderly and young? We cannot steal, so we have to use this little salary to buy bean dregs and broken rice, and cook yellow vegetable peels, barely getting by on two meals a day, like the model of a beggar, which can be seen in an instant. Moreover, the Municipal Council cares about the suffering of the people, but although we are within the concession, we have not committed any crimes. If we are considered unsanitary, we have always followed the Council's guidance. If it is for the sake of the asset-rich buildings, and we are asked to demolish our homes to live in those buildings, it would be very difficult to do so. Because our three-day shift wages are not enough to cover the rent. Even if we cannot afford to rent a house, disputes and conflicts are inevitable. If we want to return to our hometowns, there is no land to cultivate, and we do not even have travel expenses. With no home to return to, we endure the pain and seek to survive. Therefore, we implore your esteemed Federation to uphold justice for us and find a way to stop this, so that both industry and commerce can be reassured and the suffering of the weak can be alleviated."

Jardine Matheson Tugboat Salvaged by Customs 113

Wreck Buoy Installed on the Forecastle to Warn Ships to Avoid Obstructing Work

After the Jardine Matheson tugboat sank in the Huangpu River on the 4th, the Customs has installed a wreck buoy and is attempting to salvage it. The Hydrographic Office has also issued Notice No. 173, ordering all ships to pay attention. The notice states that a shipwreck has occurred off the Shanghai port in the Yangtze River estuary, and a wreck buoy has been installed for navigation. Wreck location: Within Section 9 of the Huangpu River, 283.5 degrees from the Gonghexiang Pudong Wharf flagpole, a distance of 1.5 cables (each 10 cables equals 1 nautical mile), approximately 121 degrees 31 minutes East longitude, 31 degrees 15 minutes North latitude. Current situation: The shipwrecked "St. Aulein" has its hull exposed above the water. Explanation: The symbol "wreck exposed at low tide" should be marked on the chart. Wreck buoy: Location: On the forecastle of the above-mentioned shipwreck, abbreviated as two permanent green-white (vertical). Explanation: At night, one permanent green and one permanent white light are hung vertically, green above and white below. During the day, a green flag is hung. Note: The above-mentioned shipwreck is approximately 75 feet from the edge of the wharf. Navigation notice: Explanation: All ships navigating in the area must exercise extreme caution to avoid endangering salvage work.

Factory Supervisor Interferes Leading to Tragic Accident Due to Female Worker's Mishap

Tian Yang, a woman from Yancheng who resides on Rue Robert in West Shanghai and works at the Shengyuan Silk Factory, had a three-month-old daughter named Sanmei. She brought her to the factory every day. Because the child was crying incessantly, another female worker, Zhang Sanmei, held her by the factory window to look around. A local factory supervisor named Wang Jinkang passed by and immediately interfered and pushed her. Zhang Sanmei retreated to avoid being pushed, and the child fell out of the window, landing on the ground and becoming almost a meat patty. She died instantly. Tian Yang reported the incident to the police station, and Wang Jinkang was arrested and taken to court. Prosecutor Xiao prosecuted him under Article 276, Paragraph 1 of the Criminal Code. Judge Cai opened the court to hear the case yesterday morning at 9 AM. Tian Yang was in court and requested 400 yuan in private compensation. Zhang Sanmei also testified, stating that Wang Jinkang abused his authority as a supervisor, disregarding human life. When questioned, Wang Jinkang claimed that Zhang Sanmei was distracted while looking out the window and carelessly dropped the child, blaming him. He asked for a clear investigation. The judge stated that the case required investigation and adjourned for further questioning.

Longhua Temple Monk Indecency Case Concluded 115

Sentencing on the 17th

Hongkui, the 46-year-old Sichuanese vice-abbot of Longhua Temple, also known as the chief monk, was accused of sodomy by Yang Shouchang, a fifteen-year-old temple helper. The Longhua Temple abbot, Lu Mingzhao, sent Yang to the district court, where the injury to his anus was verified. A police officer, Wu Xijun, from the Zhendong Wuxi police station, was dispatched to Longhua Temple to arrest Hongkui. Prosecutor Xie Lian filed a public indictment, stating that on the night of the 28th day of the third lunar month of this year, the defendant used violent means in his room to commit indecency against Yang Shouchang, a worker at the temple, and confined him in the room overnight. Shouchang entrusted Lu Mingzhao, a donor to the temple, to report the case. Although the defendant denied the allegations, Yang Shouchang clearly and accurately identified the details, and it was verified that Shouchang's anus did have signs of indecency. The defendant was charged with violating Article 224, Paragraph 1, and Article 302, Paragraph 1 of the Criminal Code. Yesterday morning, Judge Wu Xiangzu opened the court. The defendant hired Lawyer Yang Maomao to defend him. The judge, considering the case involved morals, prohibited spectators. However, the defendant had a written statement claiming that he was being framed for indecency, extorted, slandered, and ostracized in an attempt to seize power. He claimed that he had been at the temple for nearly three years and had served the temple. Monks Huizheng, Yueqiao, and others had repeatedly tried to take his position as vice-abbot, which they had only managed to do last month. Buddhist laymen Wang Yiting, Zhu Qinglan, Qu Yingguang, and Huang Qinglan had introduced him to become the abbot of Ruiguang Temple in Suzhou. Unexpectedly, he had provoked resentment again. Because the monk was scheduled to go to Suzhou to take over the temple on the eighth day of the fourth lunar month, they colluded with the tea boy Wang Zhaowen on the sixth day to bribe Yang Shouchang to write a letter claiming that the monk had harassed him on the twenty-second day of the third lunar month, demanding that the monk go abroad and pay 100 yuan. The monk dismissed it as absurd, and Huizheng and Yueqiao beat the monk. The monk reported it to Officer Liu of the Longhua Branch Police Station for investigation. The monk was scheduled to hold a succession ceremony on July 7, and the invitations had already been printed. Huizheng and Yueqiao were jealous and incited Yang Shouchang to falsely accuse him. He cited guest monk Ti Yong and incense-burning monk Ruyi as witnesses and requested that they be questioned on the spot. However, after reviewing the entire file, the judge found that the evidence he presented could not be adopted and therefore instructed that no questioning would take place. After a thorough examination of the cases of both parties, and after the prosecutor presented his opinion, the debate was concluded and the sentencing was scheduled for the 17th of this month. The defendant was returned to custody.

Descendants Contend Over Sun Jingchen's Estate After His Death 116

Unmarried Daughter's Estate After Death Leads to Lawsuit Among Relatives

Sun Jingchen, a wealthy merchant from Anhui, had one son and two daughters. His eldest son was named Binshan, his second daughter was named Jizhang, and his youngest daughter was named Yizhang. Binshan married Zhu Lingxian and had four children: Wenkui, Wenlan, Wenda, and Hongyu. Jizhang married into the Tao family, and Yizhang remained single. Binshan died ten years ago, leaving behind his eldest son, Wenkui, who is now twenty-two years old. Sun Jingchen also passed away in 1931. Because he left behind a large estate, there was a lawsuit, which was later settled. At that time, Sun Yizhang alone received the land and buildings at 470 Lane, Donghan Bili Road, Chang Le Li, totaling 1.182 mu, a part of the land at the corner of Tiantong Road and Wusong Road, Yang Li, totaling 2.833 mu, and 28,000 yuan in cash. On May 29th of this year, Sun Yizhang also passed away. Because she had always been single and had no adopted children, all of her estate was managed by her sister, Tao Sun Jizhang. However, Sun Wenkui and the others claimed that according to Article 1138 of the Inheritance Section of the Civil Code, they should also have inheritance rights to this estate. They hired lawyers Lin Yingqing and Shi Jun to file a lawsuit against Tao Sun Jizhang, requesting a judgment confirming that the plaintiffs had the right to inherit one-half of Sun Yizhang's estate and ordering immediate payment. Fearing that the defendant would dispose of the assets privately, they requested a preliminary execution. Judge Zhang Yuhai of the First Special Court heard the case in the Civil Division Four courtroom yesterday morning. Tao Sun Jizhang also hired lawyers Wu Zhiping and Fang Jiazhen to defend her. Her defense was that Article 1140 of the Civil Code stipulates that if an heir in the first order specified in Article 1138 dies or loses the right to inherit before the commencement of inheritance, their lineal descendants will inherit by substitution, and the third order will have no right to inherit. Therefore, the facts alleged by the plaintiffs in this case are without merit, and the plaintiffs' lawsuit should be dismissed. Both sides debated this legal issue fiercely. After Judge Zhang reviewed the documents, he declared the hearing closed and scheduled a date for sentencing.

Fujian Native Association: A Proposal to Assist Fellow Provincials in Wenzhou 120

The Wenzhou Fujian Guildhall recently faced a situation where the land on which the guildhall was located was misrepresented by the Sha Tin Commissioner stationed in Yongqing, who, with the approval of the Zhejiang Department of Finance, forcibly put it up for auction. Mr. Ding Wenzao was specially dispatched to Shanghai to appeal to the Shanghai Fujian Native Association for assistance. As this matter concerns the interests of fellow provincials, the case was brought before the Standing Committee for discussion. Mr. Ding attended the meeting and reported that the land managed by the Fujian Guildhall in Ou was purchased and donated by fellow provincial Mr. Wu and others during the Daoguang era of the former Qing Dynasty for the guildhall's use. After completing all procedures such as reporting, registration, and tax payment, the land was reclaimed from the sand and developed into its current state, requiring countless efforts and significant financial investment before the guildhall could manage it. This has been the case for over a hundred years. In the fifteenth year of the Republic of China, four mu and some odd land adjacent to the northern boundary was flooded with yellow sand. The local authorities reported it to the Reclamation Bureau for purchase. The bureau stated that although the guildhall's original land had been taxed for a long time, it was still considered official reclaimed land according to regulations and required reporting, inspection, measurement, and payment before purchase. The guildhall members, being travelers in a foreign land, dared not resist and paid the assessed land price in full, receiving a formal receipt and awaiting imperial approval for the issuance of a deed. After repeated urging, it was never completed. In the eighteenth year of the Republic of China, the Reclamation Bureau was renamed the Sha Tin Bureau. The guildhall again followed regulations and submitted the formal receipt, original purchase contract, tax receipts, and other evidence for verification, which was deemed legal, and four registration certificates were issued, allowing the guildhall to manage the property. Unexpectedly, recently, the Sha Tin Commissioner stationed in Yongqing overturned the previous case and ordered the guildhall to pay again for the land, threatening to auction it if they did not comply. The guildhall argued that they had already completed legal procedures and paid the national tax, so why should they be subjected to further extortion? They submitted a protest, but after a long time, there was no clear response, nor was there a public announcement or notice of the auction. Suddenly, on May 30th of this year, colluding with unscrupulous gentry and secretly conspiring, the commissioner auctioned the land together with the buildings on it, abusing their power and acting like robbers. Although the town chief of Chengdong and neighboring merchants and residents protested against this injustice, their power was insufficient, and nothing could be done. Therefore, the speaker was dispatched to Shanghai to appeal to the association for support. Finally, various pieces of evidence were presented. After hearing Mr. Ding's report and examining the evidence, the standing committee members of the native association all agreed that the guildhall's procedures were complete, while the Sha Tin Commissioner stationed in Yongqing, with the approval of the Department of Finance, forcibly put the land up for auction, which was a violation of the government's repeated orders to protect the property rights of organizations. It was immediately decided to send separate telegrams to the Zhejiang Provincial Government and the Department of Finance, requesting them to revoke the auction and handle the matter impartially to safeguard property rights. It is believed that the Zhejiang authorities will respect public opinion and handle the matter fairly.

Liu Haisu's Art Exhibition: The Inscriptions on Chinese Paintings Are Extremely Valuable 127

Liu Haisu, a leader of the New Art movement, is a pioneer of the New Culture Movement. Modern art has been greatly influenced by him. His oil paintings are bold and unconventional, with a touch of academic style. Europeans have already recognized him as a master. His Chinese paintings are profound in artistic conception, clear and moist in brushwork, and vigorous and unrestrained in rendering. His brushstrokes are never careless. His bold, central brushstrokes are grand and magnificent, unmatched by others. The inscriptions on each of his works are also extremely precious. The following is a brief excerpt of some of them, which should be valued by readers. No. 15, "Lone Pine on Huangshan": Chen Duxiu inscribed, "Lone pine on Huangshan, not lonely yet lonely, lonely yet not lonely. Loneliness and non-loneliness each have their own realm, each has its own use. This is not a compromise between loneliness and non-loneliness." No. 14, "Solitary Fishing in Snowy River": Cai Yuanpei inscribed, "Knowing its white, guarding its black, pondering in a pot, who can understand." No. 14, "Solitary Fishing in Snowy River": Chen Duxiu inscribed, "The painting has the meaning of Shi Gu's integration of Chinese poetry, calligraphy, and painting. In recent times, old arts have a chance to revive. Mr. Haisu is its pioneer. This painting is one that has the intention of painting." No. 73, "Autumn Willows": Cai Yuanpei inscribed, "Old trees are like grasping people, tall bamboos are my friends. If I hear the song of good birds, the sound of Sheng and Ge fill my ears." No. 94, "Huangshan Pine": Shen Enfu inscribed, "Embracing the idea that the monastery is colder than iron, I start writing Huangshan." Ancient pines, why not "leave the true face, occasionally wield a bald brush to transform into tadpoles and dragons." No. 34, "Huangshan": Cai Yuanpei inscribed, "Towering peaks, billowing clouds, between looking up and looking down, I attain great freedom." No. 54, "The True Appearance of the Mountain Lord": He Ran Li Jian inscribed, "Haiweng painted this tiger with a central brush, using the brushwork of Wang Xizhi's dragon claws. I borrow the four characters from Helu's collection and present them as praise." No. 1, "Su Mi Wang Traveling": Cai Yuanpei inscribed, "Three people, three perfections in calligraphy, poetry, and painting, a clear tour on a good day, why must it be." In the wind and snow on the bridge, the trees are lush in autumn." No. 10, "Hovering and Then Landing": He Ran Jushi inscribed, "Hovering and then landing, knowing where to stop. Living beings are driven and pursue, who can be like you?" No. 13, "Withered Tree": Ye Zuoheng inscribed, "Shaped like a bridge tree, divine and metallic inside. The gentleman's approach. Light and not." It is also said that the cold fragrance accompanies the green branches, and the friendship is as firm as gold and stone." Shen Enfu inscribed, "New comers of all images are withered, wanting to borrow a branch from the spring breeze, pitying you are not as charming as parrots, unable to use your mouth, what else can you do?" No. 52, "Autumn from Late Color": Teng Gu inscribed, "The tip of the brush hides blessings, the heart conceals a dragon, when the mood comes, a single stroke, even the creator is deceived. Lush and rustic, desolate and not heroic." No. 55, "Sea Eagle": Li Jian inscribed, "The vastness wants to examine the sky, the surging tide never returns, heroes still wear feathers, who can save the mad waves?" Each of the above masters, their people, their poems, and their calligraphy are enough to represent an era and be passed down for thousands of years, making them endlessly enjoyable to read. Liu is deeply knowledgeable, widely collected, and deeply researched, so he can shift the opportunity of history.

Salted Fish Will Be Traded in the Fish Market 128

A Discussion on Methods Will Be Held with the Salted Fish Industry on the 14th. Funds Will Be Allocated to Set Up a Retail Market to Meet the Needs of Fish Vendors

Since the establishment of the Shanghai Fish Market by the Ministry of Industry, the fish trade has been quite prosperous. The market is now planning to add a salted goods trade and build a retail market to meet the needs of fish vendors, in order to expand its business. The details are as follows:

Yesterday's Board Meeting

The Fish Market held a meeting of the Standing Directors at the Zhonghui Building on the afternoon of the ninth (yesterday), attended by Chairman Du Yuesheng, Standing Directors Fang Jiaobo, Gui Yanfang, Tang Chengzong, General Manager Wang Xiaolai, and Deputy Managers Zhu Guankai and Sun Guchen, to discuss ways to improve the fish market and other issues. The meeting lasted a long time before it adjourned.

Calling Salted Fish Industry to Join

Since the market opened on May 12, it has been during the peak season, and the fish business has been quite prosperous. However, the trade of various fish products has not yet been centralized. The reason for this is that the facilities for fish product trading are not yet complete. Therefore, currently, only seafood and river fish are traded in the market. Salted goods, which account for a large annual sales volume, have not yet joined. It is now known that the market has made arrangements for the salted goods trade. Therefore, the Board of Directors has decided that the salted goods trade will also be conducted in the market. The Board of Directors has now notified the Shanghai Salted Fish Industry Association to send representatives to the Board of Directors meeting at the Zhonghui Bank at 2:00 PM on the 14th to discuss the salted fish trade, the method of joining cooperation, and various procedural issues, so as to realize it as soon as possible.

Man from Pudong Robbed of Wages While Working as a Toilet Account Manager 130

Chen Shixue, a 33-year-old man from Pudong, living at No. 1301 Binlang Road in the West Shanghai area, was working as an account manager for a contractor of the Public Works Department's sewage cleaning business. At about 9:50 AM yesterday morning, Chen took a private car with Concession Permit No. 4158, as it was the day to distribute wages. He went to the manager's office to collect $917 in cash and then returned to the cleaning office in the same car. Unexpectedly, when the car arrived at the entrance, two robbers suddenly jumped out from the roadside and ordered Chen to hand over all the cash. Seeing the bad situation, Chen shouted "Catch the robbers!" at the entrance. The two robbers, in a panic, shot Chen in the buttocks, and he fell to the ground. The two robbers then searched Chen's pockets, robbed him of more than $800 in cash, and fled. Chen's family members and others were informed and chased after them, but the robbers had already fled without a trace. The case was immediately reported to the Gordon Road Police Station, who dispatched a car to send Chen to the hospital for treatment and dispatched detectives to search for the robbers.

Chinese Ancient Coin Society Research Meeting 131

The Chinese Ancient Coin Society held its fifth research meeting yesterday. Dozens of people, including Ding Fubao, Yi Yugong, Zhang Yicheng, Yang Kailing, and Zhang Jiliang, attended the meeting as scheduled. They each brought their collection of coins for viewing and research. In particular, the ancient coin examination manuscript of Da Xing Weng Yiquan, which was a rare and valuable treasure, was showcased. Weng collected ancient coins for decades, forming an eight-volume examination manuscript. All aspects of ancient coins, including the origin and evolution of ancient coins, ancient coin works of all dynasties, and ancient coin collectors, were extensively cited and carefully examined, harmoniously and thoroughly, standing shoulder to shoulder with Liu's Ancient Coin Garden and Li's Ancient Coin Collection. The original manuscript was annotated by Liu Yanting, who personally proofread it, but it was not published. After the Gengzi Incident, Zhao Xiaolu of Anqiu obtained the book and treasured it, unwilling to show it to others. The members of the Coin Society plan to have it engraved and printed, so that it can be widely circulated, allowing those who previously could not get it to read it. This is indeed a great event. In addition, the first issue of the Coin Society's publication, Ancient Coin Studies, has been published. The content is rich, especially with many famous works. The Medical Book Bureau and the Shanghai Magazine Company are both acting as sales agents.

Inmate in Second Special Court Detention Center Injures Head Again 135

An inmate in the Second Special District Court Detention Center on Rue Massenet in the French Concession recently demanded that officials improve treatment. As there was no result, on the morning of the eighth, inmates charged with serious crimes such as murder and robbery gathered and shouted. As the guards and wardens were unable to stop them, they reported to the French police station, which dispatched a large number of detectives to suppress the riot. The riot subsided, and the instigating inmates, including Li Shiying and twelve others, were brought to the police station for questioning. The next day, when the inmates were sent back to the detention center, they resisted orders and disrupted the situation by refusing to enter the cells. This has been reported in this newspaper. At about 8:00 PM on the afternoon of the ninth, another inmate, Chen Jinkun (sentenced to two years and six months of imprisonment for robbery), suddenly refused to eat dinner and kept complaining. The warden reported to the section chief, who ordered the inmate to be brought in for questioning. As soon as the inmate left the cell, he smashed his head against the iron door, causing injury and blood on his face. After the prison doctor bandaged his wounds, he was placed in a separate room. At 11:00 AM yesterday morning, the warden ordered two guards to escort Chen to the Second Special Court Prosecutor's Office for questioning and examination. Chief Prosecutor Qiao Wanxuan questioned him. According to Chen, he did not participate in the riot in the detention center. Last night, he was suddenly ordered to be interrogated by the warden, and he was afraid of being chained and punished, so he smashed his head against the iron door in a panic, injuring himself. It had nothing to do with anyone else, etc. Chief Qiao verified the confession and stated that since Chen had already admitted it, there was no need for further examination and ordered the guards to take him back to the detention center for detention.

Young Woman Sentenced for Bigamy 136

Four Months Imprisonment, Suspended for Two Years, Handed Over to Her Original Husband for Supervision

Wang Xiuzhen (aka Lu Wangshi aka Deng Xiuying), a young woman from Liyang, 21 years old this year, was betrothed to Lu Jincheng from the same village. She was a child bride and married him in the spring of the year before last. At the end of the year, due to famine in her hometown, she was sent to Shanghai by her aunt Lu to the home of her relative Zhang Shuifu (resident of No. 1099 Zhonghua Road), who was asked to find a job for her. Later, Zhang recommended her to work as a domestic helper, and she was brought back to her hometown in the autumn of last year. Unexpectedly, Xiuying had already been in love with someone in Shanghai and did not want to go back. Therefore, she took the opportunity to escape at the North Station and married Shen Changgen from Pudong, living with him at No. 13 Gaosheng Lane, Blue Veillée Road in the French Concession. It was not until the sixteenth of last month that Zhang Shuifu found out where she was living and reported it to the French police station, which sent detectives, including Zuo Qihong, to arrest Wang Xiuzhen and Shen Changgen's mother, Shen Huangshi, and send them to the Second Special Court. The attorney of the police department filed a public prosecution against her for bigamy. At the same time, Zhang notified her husband, Lu Jincheng, to come to Shanghai to await trial. All of this has been reported in this newspaper. The case was repeatedly heard by Judge Wang Hongxu of the Second Special Court. Lu Jincheng also testified in court, and the debate was concluded. Yesterday morning, Judge Wang ordered Wang Xiuzhen and Shen Huangshi to be brought to court and sentenced Wang Xiuzhen to four months of imprisonment, suspended for two years, and handed over to her husband Lu Jincheng for supervision. Shen Huangshi was acquitted. After the judgment, Wang Xiuzhen was taken home by her husband, and Shen Huangshi was released.

Peng Jitai Drowns While Swimming to Escape the Heat 137

Peng Jitai, a 37-year-old man from Yancheng who worked as a laborer at the Zhongshan Hardware Factory in Chenjia Ferry, this city, finished work in the evening the day before yesterday and was cooling off in front of the factory. Unable to bear the heat, he jumped into the river outside the factory to swim. Unexpectedly, he sank shortly after entering the water. The other laborers in the factory were extremely shocked and tried to retrieve him, but there was no trace. The body was found floating in the river near Chenjia Ferry at 9:00 AM the next morning. Wen Zhaoxiong, an officer from the Fifth Squadron of the Water Patrol, saw the body and ordered the local keeper, Xin Fu, to carry the body to the wharf. Later, Chen Si, a laborer from the factory, brought Peng Jitai's family to the scene. They identified the deceased as Peng Jitai. Lei Binzhang, a prosecutor from the local court, arrived at the scene and confirmed that he had indeed drowned. The family then signed a statement and took the body for burial.

Chinese Buddhist Association Cables Branches Nationwide to Strictly Prevent Traitorous Imposters Disguised as Monks 140

Recently, there have been reports of traitors in various places disguising themselves as monks in the hope of evading attention and plotting wrongdoing. The Chinese Buddhist Association believes that this matter is of great importance, not only concerning the future of the monastic community, but also greatly affecting national defense. Therefore, it has specifically cabled all branches nationwide, instructing all temples to inquire about the origins of passing monks at any time, and to pay special attention to monks traveling and wandering, selecting personnel to conduct strict investigations. If anyone is found to be suspicious, they should be reported to the local police station for handling.

Ningbo Native Association Requests Lifting of Restrictions on Siming Southern Ballads 143

Director Bao Says Further Review Pending

Since the Shanghai Telegraph Bureau, under the mandate of the Ministry of Posts and Telecommunications, began managing private radio stations and governing broadcast programs, it has spared no effort in scrutinizing scripts and reviewing broadcast lyrics. In addition to banning lewd and bizarre programs, it has also imposed time restrictions on Shanghai Operas, Siming storytelling, and Siming Southern Ballads. (Namely, regarding the Siming Southern Ballads, it is said that their lyrics are vulgar and the content is obscene, and some content is considered seditious. Therefore, it ordered the Shanghai Private Wireless Broadcasting Association, which, after receiving the order, sent a letter to the Ningbo Native Association, asking it to argue on the grounds that Siming storytelling and Siming Southern Ballads are not only elegant in style and melodious in tone but also pleasing and edifying, and are the most popular entertainment in society. It often immediately sent a special letter to the Telegraph Bureau, requesting permission to lift the restrictions, etc. This matter is related to the Electric Policy Law and affects private broadcasting and is extremely important. According to the Director of the Telegraph Bureau, Mr. Bao Keyong, during the process of reorganizing the broadcasting industry, the Telegraph Bureau must carefully consider the retention and removal of songs. This is because the underlying texts of songs often differ greatly from the lyrics sung during the broadcast. However, it is sometimes difficult to be fair in the categorization of songs. If the lyrics can be submitted to the bureau for detailed review and are confirmed not to conflict with social education, leniency will naturally be granted.)

Dai Youlin Drowns, Body Examined 144

At around 7:00 PM the day before yesterday, on the Wharf Station of Huasheng Wharf on Fair Road, Yangshupu, the wharf was crowded with cool-seekers, including over a hundred sailors from various ships. The weather was extremely hot. Dai Youlin, an 18-year-old Hubei native working as a cook on the Dehe Steamer, saw many of his colleagues from Guangdong and Tianjin swimming in the river. On a whim, he also jumped in to play. Due to his poor swimming skills, he drowned. His swimming companions quickly dragged him onto the wharf, but he had swallowed too much water and was unconscious. He was taken to Renji Hospital by police vehicle No. 31. Half an hour later, he died. His body was taken to the autopsy station on Linglun Road. Subsequently, his cousin, Dai Shaoqing, was notified and learned that Chen Fa, a cook of the same ship and from the same hometown, had pushed him into the water, causing the tragedy. He reported the situation to the Huishan Police Station, which dispatched Chinese detective Cui Chengke to take Chen into custody at the police station. Yesterday morning, he was sent to the Third Criminal Court of the First Special District Court. The lawyer of the Public Works Department, Zhang Shizhu, stated that Chen Fa denied the charges at the police station and requested temporary detention for further investigation. Following Dai Shaoqing's account of the incident, Chen Fa was questioned and insisted that the deceased was not pushed by him but had done it himself, requesting judgment. Judge Zhong Qing ordered him to be detained pending further investigation. Tang, the prosecutor from the court, arrived at the scene and confirmed that Dai Youlin had indeed died from drowning before death. The body was handed over to Dai Shaoqing, the deceased's cousin, to claim and arrange the funeral after signing a guarantee.

Letter 153

To the Editor: Today (the 10th), in the local news column of your newspaper, there was an item about Yao Guangding, the chief of the Ximen Public Security Bureau, being accused of dereliction of duty. After reading it, I was extremely surprised. It was found that on the afternoon of the 2nd of this month, the plaintiff, Qiao Jinquan, filed a complaint against tenants Li Jiatong and Liang Jinshi for owing rent and relying on brute force to estimate the value, etc., and attached two rent books and property tax receipts. After investigation, it was found to be true. According to Article 14 of the Shanghai Municipal Housing Lease Rules, a police officer was dispatched to the case and ordered the bureau to question the officers, approve the plaintiff to directly prosecute in court, and the defendant to provide bail, or be detained without bail, etc. Unexpectedly, after the defendant was sentenced, he sought bail everywhere, but could not find it all day. On the 4th of this month, he prepared a document and submitted it to the Public Security Bureau for verification. Not only was there no detention for eight days, but there was also no illegal acceptance of the case. This is all documented and cannot be fabricated. In addition to filing a lawsuit against the plaintiff for false accusation, I am sending you a letter outlining the handling of this case, and I hope you will grant a correction. Sincerely, Shanghai Municipal Public Security Bureau Ximen Branch, July 10.
