Page 16

Sports News

Record of the World Games Delegation's Journey 155

Special Correspondent of the Central News Agency, Feng Youzhen (Second Letter, Continued)

Fellowship on the Same Boat

Today is the last day of June. The gloomy weather has increased the terror at sea. The mail ship is forging ahead proudly in the Chinese Sea. Although it has not encountered any major storms, it is always a bit uneasy. At lunchtime, I counted the seats at the table and found that fifteen or sixteen seats were empty. People without sailing experience probably only curse such weather. After lunch, there was a heavy rain, and the sky cleared up. Everyone was lying on the rattan chairs on the deck, enjoying the breeze and the cool. Several people with sailing experience brought a lot of preserved mustard greens and pickled vegetables before departure. It is said that these two things are more effective in treating seasickness than any medicine. So everyone scrambled to eat them, as if they had obtained sweet rain in a severe drought.

At 5:00 PM, the ship held a lifeboat drill. All the ship's staff, sailors, and passengers participated in the drill. The whistle emitted a short roar, and the alarm bells rang continuously. Everyone seemed to be in real danger, rushing to their rooms to put on their life jackets and then running to the designated deck to assemble. The ship's staff guided and corrected those who wore their life jackets incorrectly. After five minutes, the whistle emitted a signal indicating that the danger had passed, and everyone was dismissed. Such a drill increases everyone's knowledge of what to do in case of danger, which is very meaningful.

The Conte Verde has probably set a new record for the number of Chinese passengers it has carried since its sailing history. In addition to the delegation of more than 100 athletes, there are 33 members of the World Games European Tour organized by the China Travel Service. There are also 20-30 other compatriots going to Europe, such as Mr. Pan Huaguo, the deputy military attaché of the Chinese Embassy in Germany, Mr. Deng Shuren, who is going to Germany to study military affairs, and Mr. Luo Zhijian, a famous tennis player. In total, there are more than 200 people.

Three members of the European Tour of the China Travel Service will board the ship in Singapore. Among the remaining 30, there is one each from Peiping and Nanking, three from Hong Kong, and twenty-five from Shanghai. The one from Peiping is the well-known Mr. Jiang Yong from the legal profession, who was elected as the leader of the tour. Their route is to visit Italy, Austria, Czechoslovakia, Germany, the Netherlands, England, Belgium, France, and Switzerland, and then return to China via Italy. After finishing his business, Mr. Jiang Yong must also go to Austria to attend the World Judicial Conference.

Everyone felt that during this 20-day sea voyage, they should organize and connect with each other. So they initiated the organization of the "World Games Same Boat Fellowship," and elected Mr. Jiang as the president. Nine staff members were elected. Hao Gengsheng, Yuan Dunli, and a reporter were elected on the side of the athlete delegation; lawyer Liu Zhen, doctor Wang Bichen, and Deng Bingquan, a staff member of the travel group, were elected on the side of the European tour; and the remaining three were Mr. Pan Huaguo, Deng Shuren, and Xue Lutan. After passing Singapore, the organizing committee will decide on the method of fellowship. Who says that we Chinese do not have the ability to organize?

High Spirits for Recreation

July 1st, the weather is clear, and the brilliance of the sun shines on the sea, reflecting golden ripples, which is truly beautiful. Everyone is very excited and active, no longer as depressed as yesterday.

Morning exercises were held for half an hour starting at 7:00 AM, and will be held on time every day thereafter. The recreation committee initiated a chess competition. The participants are Shu Hong, Leng Peigen, Lin Shaozhou, Wang Shoufang, Liu Changchun, Qian Yiqin, Song Junfu, Jiang Zhende, Wu Demao, Dai Shuguo, Zheng Huaixian, Peng Wenyu, Zhang Erding, and a reporter, a total of fourteen people. The competition uses an elimination system, and the opponents must play three games. A winning game gets two points, and a draw gets one point each. The first to get four points wins. The preliminary round was held this morning. It is scheduled to produce the champion on July 4th. Judging from the situation, the champion will probably be Wu Demao and Lin Shaozhou. After the chess competition is over, a Go championship will also be held. During the long journey, this kind of recreation increases everyone's interest.

In order to make everyone know a little German and reduce the language difficulties after arriving in Germany, the discussion committee started teaching German from today. German consultant Kurt, translator Mei Fuxiang, tour member Wu Zheng, and doctor Huang Yuankai, etc., taught in four classes. Each class had a dozen or so people participating.

In the entire group, more than ten people have been sick in the past two days. Some are because of improper diet, eating unaccustomed food that caused diarrhea. Some are because the room is hot, so they slept with the electric fan on and caught a cold. Doctor Huang Yuankai is extremely busy, but fortunately, none of them are serious. They are all better after taking some medicine.

The recreation committee has scheduled to hold the first recreation party tomorrow night. The venue is the music room in the first class cabin. All Chinese and Western passengers on the ship are invited to participate in addition to the delegation. The recreation program includes a formal singing of the Party song and a speech, as well as a chorus of all the female members, a speech by Wang Huaiqi and Jiang Zhende, a martial arts performance by the martial arts team, and a funny dance by Fu Baolu and Chen Baoqiu. At that time, there will definitely be many jokes.

Tomorrow (the 2nd) morning at 9:00 AM, we can arrive in Singapore. The journey of 1,451 nautical miles will soon come to an end. It is said that the overseas Chinese there will hold a welcome meeting. Everyone is preparing to participate and wants to visit. As for the situation in Singapore, I will have to report it in four days, when I arrive in Colombo. (To be continued)

China National Health Education Society Annual Meeting Opens 162

Chairman Zhou Fohai Reports and Exhibition Held

(Zhenjiang Special Dispatch) The first annual meeting of the China National Health Education Society opened at the Zhenjiang Medical and Political College yesterday (the 10th) at 3 PM. The weather was extremely hot that day, but the participation of members from within and outside the province was exceptionally enthusiastic. A total of more than 140 members and over 100 guests were tallied. Vice Chairman Zhou Fohai represented the interim chairman. The ribbon-cutting ceremony at the exhibition hall was performed by Madam Yang Shuhui, wife of Zhou Fohai. After the opening ceremony, a preparatory meeting was held immediately. In the evening, the Jiangsu Provincial Government hosted a public banquet. The general meeting will continue tomorrow (the 11th). The details of today are recorded as follows:

Society Members

Yu Hongsheng, Hu Dingan, Shao Xiangyi, Li Ziheng, Wang Jiaying, Liang, Zhou Fohai, Gao Meifang, Xiao Hu, Zhang Ligang, Hu Songshan, Xu Jinsheng, Yu Dawang, Yu Dazhun, Zhang Dongxu, Tian Wudou, Shen Zhaoyi, Chu Heng, Liu Youzhong, Yu Zongxuan, Chen Bangxian, Song Guikun, Chen Dinghong, Yi Junzuo, Xu Shaodi, Chen Wanli, Xu Zuyi, Jiang Qingyun, Xu Jihong, Zhou Shilu, Zhang Jia, Gao Yiyi, Ye Suzhou, Niu Changyao, Tang Zhe, Liu Jian, Wang Qizhang, Xu Xiaochu, Yu Songyun, Zhou Mengbai, Xie Yunshou, Guo Renji, Lei Li, Cao Chu, etc., totaling 141 persons.

Opening Ceremony Held

The opening ceremony commenced at 3 PM. After the ceremony was performed, Vice Chairman Zhou Fohai of the Annual Meeting Preparatory Committee delivered a report as chairman. Chairman Chen Guofu was ill in Beijing, so Zhou read the opening address on his behalf. Zhou himself then gave a speech, stating briefly that the Health Education Society had been established for nearly a week, and due to the short time, there were no good achievements yet. The report on the past year, such as the preparatory process, member solicitation, and business plans, etc., has been printed in a special booklet and will not be repeated here. Secretary-General Hu Dingan reported that Executive Director Chen Guofu sent a telegram to excuse himself due to illness and to congratulate the conference. In addition, more than ten congratulatory telegrams were received from the National Economic Commission, etc. Subsequently, Lei Zhen, representing the Ministry of Education, briefly described the Ministry's promotion of medical education. Zhu Jiqing, representing the Ministry of Health, Bian Zhongmeng, representing the Provincial Party Headquarters, Luo Shishi, representing the Provincial Government, Wang Qizhang, representing the National Medical Association, and Xu Xiaochu, representing the Shanghai Western Medicine Industry Association, successively delivered speeches. At 4:30 PM, the ceremony concluded and a photograph was taken.

Ribbon Cutting Ceremony Held

After the opening ceremony, Madam Yang Shuhui, wife of Zhou Fohai, performed the ribbon-cutting ceremony, accompanied by Miss Hu Meiyi, daughter of Secretary-General Hu Dingan. A colored rope was stretched across the entrance of the exhibition hall at the Medical and Political College. Madam Yang held silver scissors, and Miss Hu held a tray. After the colored rope was cut, members entered in an orderly fashion, toured for a week, and were given printed materials and medicines by various exhibiting manufacturers. Afterwards, several cars went to the exhibition hall at the People's Education Center for the ribbon-cutting ceremony, which was the same as before.

Preparatory Meeting

At 5 PM in the afternoon, a preparatory meeting was held, chaired by Executive Director Ye Huzhong. After his speech, Secretary-General Hu Dingan reported on the preparations for the annual meeting. Subsequently, Shao Xiangyi, convener of the proposal review committee, reported on the proposal review process. A total of 85 proposals were received. The review result divided them into: Health Education Administration Group, Youth Health Group, Public Health Group, Children's Health Group, and Society Affairs Group, and it was decided to have the members re-review them. At 8 PM in the evening, a review meeting was held. The motion to elect the presidium was passed, and it was decided to elect Chen Guofu, Zhou Fohai, Ye Suzhou, Cao Chu, Xu Shaodi, Shao Xiangyi, and Weng Zhilong as the seven members of the presidium.

Hubei Province to Discontinue Education College 164

To Establish Training Institute for Township Officials

All Students Telegraph Ministry of Education in Opposition

Hankou Navigation News: The Hubei Provincial Education College was established in October of the 20th year of the Republic (1931) when He Chengjun was in charge. It was established based on the resolutions of the Second National Education Conference and the urgent needs of the province. Although its organization belongs to the independent college within the university education system, its content is of a special nature. It is divided into two major systems: rural education and agricultural education, with a graduation period of four years. There are three specialized courses: rural normal school, public education, and agricultural education, with a graduation period of two years. If necessary, various special training classes are set up to create talents for rural construction, in order to achieve the goal of rural revitalization. Since its establishment, a total of 128 graduates from the specialized courses have been assigned to work in rural areas. Recently, the provincial government decided to discontinue the college and establish a training institute for township officials in order to actively improve rural construction. On June 17th, the Department of Education issued a clear order to discontinue the college, which aroused the opposition of all students. On August 8th, all students went to the Department of Education to petition for the withdrawal of the order and did not disperse overnight. On the 9th, Director Cheng Qibao personally met with them and promised to convey their opinions to the chairman. The students were satisfied and left the hall to await orders.

Education Bureau Orders Schools to Prohibit Collection of Graduation Certificate Fees 171

Severe Punishment for Those Who Dare to Violate

The Shanghai Municipal Education Bureau issued an order to public primary and secondary schools, stating: "It has been found that the fees that schools should charge students are all stipulated, and no extra fees should be collected. However, according to reports, at the end of the semester, some schools are charging graduation fees from graduating students, some as high as more than two yuan, which is truly astonishing. An investigation should be conducted immediately. In the future, schools should not charge any fees from graduating students other than the one-corner stamp tax that should be affixed to secondary school certificates in accordance with regulations. Severe punishment will be imposed on those who dare to violate this order after investigation. All schools are hereby ordered to comply."

Ministry of Education Issues Standards for Sanitary Facilities in Primary Schools (1) 172

On the 9th, the Ministry of Education issued a circular to the Education Departments and Bureaus of all provinces and cities, stating: "The Provisional Standards for Sanitary Facilities in Rural Primary Schools and the Provisional Standards for Sanitary Facilities in Urban Primary Schools have been formulated separately by the Ministry. In addition to being promulgated and distributed separately by ministerial order, two copies of the standards are enclosed, and you are instructed to forward them to all subordinate primary schools for compliance. This order."

Provisional Standards for Sanitary Facilities in Rural Primary Schools

A. Goals: 1. To cultivate children's hygiene concepts through educational methods; 2. To protect children's health by using simple sanitary facilities; 3. To promote public health by centering on children's healthy lives.

B. Organization: Each school should have a teacher who has received hygiene training, under the guidance of the County Health Education Committee, to be responsible for the school's health affairs. The technical work on hygiene should be assisted by the local health authorities.

C. Funding: Each school should include school health funding in the budget. If necessary, a hygiene fee may be charged to students, but at most one dime per student per semester. Schools with fewer than 40 students should have an initial expense of 5 yuan and an annual recurring expense of 12 yuan. This should be doubled for schools with more than 40 and fewer than 100 students.

D. Scope of Work: 1. Health Education: Teachers in each school should conduct health education for children based on the Ministry's issued primary school civic training standards, common sense for lower and middle grades, and natural science curriculum standards for upper grades, paying attention to the development of children's hygiene knowledge and skills, the formation of habits, and the training of attitudes, and should contact families to promote children's health. At the same time, all sanitary facilities should be fully utilized to enhance the effectiveness of health education. 2. Health Examination: Each school should, to the extent possible, entrust the local health authorities to conduct health examinations for children. 3. Vaccination: New students must be vaccinated against smallpox upon admission. At the same time, the local health authorities should be entrusted to carry out vaccination. 4. Simple Treatment: Teachers who have received hygiene training should provide children with the following simple treatments. To the extent possible, efforts should be made to popularize it to the general public in the local area: Eye diseases, Ringworm and impetigo, Tinea capitis, External skin injuries, Skin ulcers, Syncope. 5. Sanitary Equipment: Record forms, Vaccination records, Cleanliness records, Simple treatment records, Self-reporting and monthly (attached separately), Medicines and equipment: Determined according to local conditions, with simplicity, economy, practicality and safety as the principles (detailed list attached separately), Hygiene habit chart (published by the Ministry of Health), Statutory nine types of infectious diseases in the series (published by the Ministry of Health), Other reference books. Items 1 and 2 above must be equipped. The rest can be set up according to the school's financial resources.

Provisional Standards for Sanitary Facilities in Urban Primary Schools

A. Goals: 1. To cultivate children's healthy living habits; 2. To use modern scientific medical facilities to improve children's health and prevent children's diseases; 3. To make the school's sanitary facilities affect children's families, and to promote the realization of children's healthy living environment through the connection and cooperation between schools and families; 4. To enhance children's basic knowledge and skills about health.

B. Organization: Each school or several schools jointly organize a school health education committee, with the principal, teachers, doctors, and nurses as members, to handle all matters related to school health.

C. Personnel: Including principals, teachers, doctors, nurses, assistants, and children. Doctors and nurses are set up jointly by one or several schools. Generally, there should be one full-time doctor, two nurses, and one assistant for every 5,000 children.

D. Funding: The school health funding for primary schools should be based on an average of one yuan per student per year in principle. The sources are as follows: 1. School administrative funding (the school should include this expense in the budget); 2. Student health fees (primary school students should pay a health fee of two dimes per semester).

E. Scope of Work: 1. Health Education: Health Teaching: (1) Compilation of Teaching Materials: Hygiene in primary schools is not an independent subject. Knowledge and skills related to hygiene are incorporated into the teaching of common sense and natural science subjects, and habits are incorporated into training in civic training. The compilation of teaching materials and the implementation of items should be carried out in accordance with the Ministry's issued common sense, natural science curriculum standards and primary school civic training standards. (2) Teaching Equipment: Each school should have the following equipment for hygiene teaching. Regarding civic aspects, Hygiene habit posters, Physiological hygiene models, Health and economic charts (published by the Ministry of Health), Design drawings of home and school arrangements, Personal cleanliness comparison table, Group cleanliness comparison table (self-made), Visual acuity test chart, Actual age calculation table (published by the Ministry of Health). Regarding common sense and natural science aspects, Physiological anatomy chart (published by Commercial Press), Road safety chart, Infectious disease chart, Mosquito and fly models, Comparison table of food nutrients, Models of typhoid, diphtheria, cholera infectious diseases, Models of scabies, tinea capitis, trachoma, etc., Tooth model, Suitable dietary standards for children, Chart of sexual evolution, School hygiene chart, Children's hygiene supplementary reading materials (published by the Ministry of Health), Other: Weighing scale, Stature measuring device, Other. 2. Discipline: (1) Attitude Training: Teachers should lead by example, implement individual training and group guidance at fixed times or take advantage of opportunities. (2) Habit Formation: Teachers should contact parents to lead by example and cultivate children's healthy living habits, especially paying attention to healthy living habits such as nutrition, activity, and rest. 3. Activities: (1) Hygiene Team Organization and Training: Primary and secondary school children should be uniformly organized into hygiene teams. The organizational and training methods are attached separately. (2) Other Hygiene Activities: Primary and secondary school children should take the opportunity to visit public health facilities and participate in other hygiene activities. 4. Family Liaison: (1) Parent-Teacher Talks: Teachers or nurses should invite parents to the school for talks when new students undergo health examinations and when old students have special health problems. (2) Home Visits: When correcting children's shortcomings and discovering major diseases, teachers or nurses should visit each home and pay attention to the inspection and improvement of the family environment. (3) Family Communication: Parents should be informed of the children's health status at the end of each semester, and occasional events should also be communicated and discussed frequently. (4) Parent-Teacher Meetings, etc.: Parent-teacher meetings or other exhibitions and performances should be held every semester to invite parents to visit the school's sanitary facilities and children's hygiene activities and achievements, and to discuss family and school hygiene contact and cooperation issues. 2. Health Examination: (1) Physical Examination: All new students should undergo physical examinations within the first semester after entering school. Thereafter, except for the first grade as new students, re-examinations should be carried out once in the fourth and sixth years. If the doctor deems it necessary, examinations may be carried out at any time. Before the implementation of the examination, the homeroom teacher should briefly explain the health examination situation to the children and fill in the various health conditions of each child in the health record. The homeroom teacher should assist in the examination. (To be continued)

Commercial News

Yarn and Cotton Market: Multi-Party Manipulation Leads to Surge, Old Cotton Raises Two Yuan 173

—Rumors of Preparing for a Squeeze—

In the cotton market this morning, due to the surge in Indian cotton, the bulls took the opportunity to vigorously push up prices. Old cotton rose by more than six dimes. In the afternoon, it was rumored that the bulls had formed a considerable organization and were planning to squeeze old cotton. The market was filled with buying momentum, and the atmosphere was extremely tense. July and August futures jumped by more than one yuan. Although there was no certainty about this year's new cotton harvest, some bears continued to sell, but they were ultimately no match for the strong buying momentum, which also lifted prices by eight or nine dimes. Old cotton for this month broke through 48 yuan, and new cotton for three months all broke through the 44 yuan mark.

This Month Surpasses Eight Yuan Mark

The spot cotton market opened this morning. Although the rise in American cotton was stable, the situation was still firm. Supported by American cotton, Indian cotton surged by 4.25 to 10 rupees. In the spot cotton market, old cotton for July and August had insufficient gains yesterday, so the bulls engaged in pushing up prices, surging by six dimes to six dimes and five points. The situation in the second session remained firm, and the third closing was stable. However, because some traders were dumping new cotton, and the bulls were focusing on old cotton and did not show significant buying interest in new cotton, the market was relatively stable, rising only by five points to one dime. The second session in the afternoon saw rumors of bulls aggressively buying up old cotton in a squeeze. July and August jumped by one yuan, and new cotton was pulled up by two, four, and five to six dimes. In the third session, July continued to rise by one dime, and August rose slightly by one dime. New cotton rose slightly by one or two dimes. At the close, the momentum continued, with old cotton continuing to rise by two dimes and five points to four dimes and five points, and new cotton continuing to rise by two dimes and five points to four dimes. Shen Bao Women's Special Section

Summer Vacation Labor and Women 187

— Chen Danxing

The long summer vacation of more than two months has now begun. Whether on the streets, at the docks, or at the train stations, there are traces of female students, happily carrying luggage and books, embarking on their journeys and returning to their hometowns. After half a year of studying, living a rigid and boring school life, one cannot help but feel weary. Everyone now holds the idea of spending a comfortable summer. At home, there is no restriction of classes, and they do not have to worry about all the trivial matters themselves. These women think that as modern, educated, new women, they disdain to do those trivial housework. Besides reading and attending classes, it's all about "enjoying life."

This thinking is widespread, so the mistake is also widespread. I believe the meaning of summer vacation is not at all to call the students—including the female students—to go home to—"escape the heat" or "enjoy life," but precisely to provide a suitable opportunity to experience life education in practice, away from the somewhat empty and abstract book education. From practicing small household chores to helping directly or indirectly with sanitation work and reforming living habits in rural towns and villages. Currently, many so-called new-style women often look down on the work that mothers or maids do, and even more so on the simple forms in their hometowns, and think they inherently belong to the city. To manage matters in rural towns and villages is considered extremely boring. What is especially strange is that some new-style women themselves think that they are unwilling to do these things, but they hope that others will do them, while they themselves lie on rattan chairs and comment. They have not thought about whether they will be subject to even harsher comments!

"Why do you want to study?" Everyone will answer this question quickly, either to be the main force in the women's movement, or to be a female politician, or to be determined to serve society. No one would say: After I study, I plan to be a parasite, a freeloader in society. Aspirations are certainly great, and ambitions are certainly extraordinary, but how should we begin to lead the masses, serve society, and work for the country? Do we need to have some practice beforehand? I think; from trivial to great undertakings, from local to the whole society, that is the inevitable trend.

Female students who have returned home for the summer vacation, do not waste this opportunity! Know that stealing time to enjoy life requires no practice. The labor you do now is the foundation for your future ambition to put into practice.

Marriage Age of British Women 188

— Pei Yu

The period of youth is the period of love, which can be said to be known to all, but in present-day England, the period of love is no longer the period requiring marriage, and it has become a country where late marriages are prevalent. According to the statistical reports of the census, in 1871, the marriage rate of every thousand 20-year-old women was 133.7. In 1921 it was 114.4; in 1931 it was 106.5. In 1871, the marriage rate of every thousand women between the ages of 25 and 30 was 85.9, in 1921 it was 100, and in 1931 it was 96.9. The statistics for men are as follows: In 1871, the marriage rate of every thousand 20-year-old men was 122.4, in 1921 it was 94.4; in 1931 it was 72.5. The marriage rate of men between the ages of 25 and 30 was: In 1871 it was 119.3, in 1921 it was 161.1, and in 1931 it was 140.8. One point to note here is that in 1871, the remarriage rate of every thousand 20-year-old widows was 170.5, which was higher than the marriage rate of women of the same age. In 1871, the remarriage rate of every thousand 20-year-old widowers was 229.0, which was a rapid increase compared to the marriage rate of the same age.

If you want to notice the changes between now and the Victorian era, just look at the British royal family. Queen Victoria was married before the age of twenty-one, and the prince she married was not older than she was. Her great-grandson, the Duke of Gloucester (referring to the younger brother of the English new Emperor Edward VIII, who married in early November of last year), did not marry until he was thirty-five, and the Duchess was also thirty-four years old. In the Victorian era, an unmarried woman at the age of twenty-five was already considered old; by the age of twenty-eight, she was an old maid. A man aged thirty-five or forty would look for a wife among girls aged eighteen to twenty-one, and a man of this age would likely be taking a second wife. Now, husbands and wives can be called friends and travel companions, and sometimes they can be called co-workers. Whether living in a palace or a cottage, husband and wife are partners in life. Late marriage can help to create an ideal union and find an ideal partner. This is one of the results of changing social conditions, undoubtedly created for personal happiness. But scientists and politicians are very concerned about this situation. They believe that this is one of the important reasons for the decline in the birth rate.

In 1881, the population of England and Wales was 26 million, and there were 900,000 births. In 1931, the population was 40 million, but there were only 630,000 births. Sir Arnold Wilson told the British Association: "The time when our population is static will not be long, perhaps it will decrease, and the late marriage of women is one of the direct reasons. Poverty is not a factor in the decline in the birth rate. The standard of living that married men and women desire is a big factor. When people carefully choose a car or a stroller, they always choose a car, which implies the desire to reduce the number of children." In short, people now have to think carefully before getting married. Cottage romance is not as common as it used to be, unless the cottage has a good gas stove, electric broom, electric iron, and labor-saving equipment in the kitchen. It is not to say that there is no longer any spiritual love, and everything must be based on material enjoyment. The reality is that people are more knowledgeable and have a wider range of knowledge. Therefore, marriage often has to wait until around the age of thirty. Now that the standard of living and enjoyment has increased, the concept of age is very different from before, and no one would think that a thirty-year-old woman is old. Moreover, women are no longer slaves. They have freedom, and they have greater opportunities to find careers to support themselves. We should not only not oppose late marriage, but also help them meet all their needs and create an independent spirit.

Marriage, Hygiene, and Health 189

— Hua Ling

When discussing women's issues today, everyone immediately brings up sexual liberation, freedom of occupation, equality of life, and so on, while few people pay attention to issues such as hygiene and health in marriage. This is truly a very unfortunate phenomenon. Recently, the health authorities of a certain city announced that during physical examinations of newly admitted female students at a girls' school, it was discovered that some had congenital syphilis, and some had directly contracted syphilis. Most of the female students nowadays come from families above the poverty line and have a certain level of knowledge. Yet, they still suffer from congenital or acquired syphilis. It is not difficult to imagine how rampant this bacteria is. Therefore, I feel that in this age when women have already won freedom of marriage, it is essential to not neglect the health and hygiene of the prospective spouse before getting married.

In order to prohibit marriages between Germans and Jews, Germany issued several regulations regarding marriage. However, these regulations, in practice, are not only about prohibiting German-Jewish marriages. Some of the rules also apply to marriages between Germans, For example, if one or both parties are not physically healthy, such as suffering from syphilis, lung disease, or other illnesses, and cannot provide a health certificate from a doctor, they are prohibited from marrying. This is something extremely worthy of consideration because children born to parents with serious illnesses naturally cannot become healthy citizens. The German nation is known for its excellence, so they are greatly concerned about producing unhealthy citizens. China is a weak country. If we continue to follow this path, allowing men and women with syphilis or lung disease to marry, what kind of face will the Chinese nation have in the future?

Based on the above reasons, I feel that before marriage, both parties should ask a doctor to examine them and prove that they have no syphilis, no lung disease, or other serious illnesses. If one party is found to have a serious illness, the marriage should be postponed or even canceled to avoid infection and lifelong regret. If, in fact, due to intense love, they cannot bring themselves to take decisive action, then I believe it is necessary to strictly implement birth control to prevent the children born from being innocently plunged into unfortunate fates. This benefits both the nation and the family. Group weddings are popular in various cities now. I think it would be possible to stipulate clearly that all those applying to join a group wedding must submit a doctor's certificate proving that they have no diseases that could affect the health and hygiene of their partners before they are allowed to join. This may seem like a harsh rule now, but besides this method, who can set an example and promote it?

Furthermore, most ordinary women nowadays lack sufficient knowledge about venereal diseases. Often, wives whose husbands are infected do not even realize it. By the time they are infected by their husbands, although they feel pain, they are ashamed to seek help, leading to unimaginable consequences. This is extremely common. In such cases, I urge women to have some knowledge of venereal diseases to monitor their husbands' health and hygiene, and to protect themselves. If they are infected by their husbands, they must not let it spread. They must seek medical treatment as soon as possible to avoid producing children with congenital diseases, and then regret it.

Women of New Fuzhou in Nanyang 190

— Zhu Junyi

New Fuzhou is far away in the southern islands, south of the Chinese South Sea, on the northern coast of Borneo. Thirty years ago, it was nothing more than barren and remote land. After the Guangxu period of the late Qing Dynasty, overseas Chinese began to cultivate there. These people were all Fujian compatriots who accidentally found this barren land while seeking a place to live overseas. Because the scenery was pleasant, the weather was warm, and the land was fertile, they settled there, intending to reside there permanently. Later, because eight or nine out of ten were from Fuzhou, the place was named New Fuzhou. The entire region has no more than 30,000 residents, and the number of women is less than one-third of the number of men. They are in an unequal position to men. The strong and middle-aged are diligent in their work, but the elderly and young women are very few.

Apart from the elderly and young women working at home, eight out of ten middle-aged women work in rubber plantations, because the area is planted with rubber trees, which are very lush. The local overseas Chinese all depend on this for their livelihoods. They definitely have the ability to be economically self-sufficient, and they have more than enough. Therefore, their assistance to the family's livelihood is not shallow, which is an advantage that women in the country do not have.

They work about ten hours a day, all toiling under the scorching sun. The work process is as follows: first, use a knife to cut the rubber tree bark. Then, use a cup to collect the flowing rubber. Pour the rubber from each cup into a bucket, and then transport the rubber from the bucket to another place, where it is mixed with chemicals to solidify it. Then, use a machine to roll it into sheets of rubber, and then wash it. That is the end of a day's work. Then, they can go to the river in groups, happily bathe, and prepare dinner.

They continue like this day after day, unless there is a heavy rain in the evening or morning. Otherwise, there is no chance to rest. However, there are also a small number who are devout Christians and must strictly observe the Sabbath. Therefore, they can rest on Sundays, but they have to sit motionlessly in the church for more than ten hours, which is not as free and relaxed as working in the rubber plantation!

As for how much they earn for such hard work, in the past, when the cost of living was low, each woman could earn about 30 to 40 yuan a month. However, the current situation is very different. The reason is that the price of rubber has fallen sharply, and everyone is rushing to do this business. It is difficult to even maintain their daily lives. If there are illnesses or unfortunate events like weddings or funerals, there is no money to spend.

"Three meals a day, just seeking to fill the stomach" is their saying about food, because there is no delicious food to buy there. As for what they wear, most of it is made of coarse cloth. Women inherently have a love for beauty, but they do not like to dress up and have no extravagant habits. This aspect is admirable!

Their marriage issues are enforced by their parents. The children dare not resist at all, and the goal of marriage is based on money and social status. Whoever can pay a large bride price can take the woman as their own. The author has lived there for ten years, and has heard and seen that not a single woman has not been engaged under this buying-and-selling marriage system. As for the reasons, there are several: Because there are more men than women, there are not enough to distribute. Because most of the men who are engaged are over 30 years old. Women can work and reduce the burden on men. Women have not received adequate education and lack knowledge. There is no reason to resist. Therefore, if education can be popularized soon, this autocratic marriage system may gradually be eliminated.

Discussion on Establishing a Correspondence School for Housewives 192

— Zhiyun

The subjects taught in general schools are mostly Chinese language, foreign languages, mathematics, physics, chemistry, history, geography, and so on. Specialized schools specialize even more in various specialized subjects. This kind of education is obviously not suitable for women in our country, who make up the absolute majority and whose way out is marriage. Although some girls' schools also have courses such as sewing and cooking, these useful courses do not receive as much attention as other general courses, which is also an obvious fact. This situation may be similar in the United States, so not long ago, there was the creation of "bride schools" to train women who are about to become brides with some common sense in handling household affairs. The organization and curriculum of these bride schools cannot be fully understood, so it is impossible to study them here. However, I always feel that handling household affairs is a complex matter, and it cannot be successfully trained through classroom education lasting only a few months or weeks. Moreover, there are many ways to manage a home that cannot be understood and appreciated simply by reading notes and writing notes. For the sake of practicality, I feel that it is necessary to create a "Correspondence School for Housewives."

The Correspondence School for Housewives can be divided into several groups, such as "Sewing," "Cooking," "Infant Care," "Husband Management," "Servant Management," "Family Hygiene," "Socializing," "Birth Control," "Family Reading Materials," etc. Several groups do not need to be concentrated in one place. For example, the "Sewing Group" can be entrusted to a clothing company. The "Infant Care Group" can be handled by a childcare organization. The "Family Reading Materials Group" can be jointly managed by a bookstore or newsstand. The work of each group can be entrusted to a specialized organization. The so-called correspondence school does not need any grand equipment or a large number of clerks and secretaries. The responsibility of the school is only to contact reliable branch offices and guide correspondents to the appropriate place to inquire and forward various correspondence letters. If the work develops, it can naturally compile correspondence publications, publicly publish some valuable questions and answers from a certain period, and distribute or sell them to housewives in each family. In a considerable period of time, it can also create correspondence statistics for each group and study the needs, development, and improvement of that curriculum.

If this kind of correspondence school is really established, I think that new housewives or mothers with newborn children in each family will feel extremely happy and convenient. If there are occasional household management problems that are difficult to solve, they only need to write a letter to the correspondence school, and the correspondence school will forward it to a certain group, or write directly to a certain group to inquire, or call a certain group to inquire directly, and they can get answers and guidance. This is naturally much better than asking neighbors for advice and getting irresponsible or unreasonable guidance, or gaining experience through failure. Therefore, I feel that the establishment of this kind of correspondence school is extremely worthy of discussion at present. There is no shortage of enthusiastic men and women in Shanghai who care about the happiness of women! I think this may be realized in the near future and benefit housewives who have no home management experience.

Interview with Ms. Dai Yi, Wife of Wu Yun Chu 193

— Ji Ping

Devoted to factory affairs, diligent and hardworking all year round, disregarding personal enjoyment; Providing relief to the poor, nurturing students, all for the benefit of society!

A few days ago, the newspapers reported that the International Labor Olympic Games awarded a first-class prize to Mr. Wu Yun Chu of our country. This is a very honorable thing. Mr. Wu is a leader in the domestic chemical industry. It is not known how much effort he has put in to earn this medal, which is much more valuable than our domestic first-class Caiyu Medal. Moreover, he represents the Chinese people in winning international honor, which means that he is gaining face for everyone, so it is worth congratulating. I remember Mr. Zhang Boling once said that China has two chemical industrialists, namely "Wu in the South and Fan in the North." Wu in the South is Mr. Wu Yun Chu, and Fan in the North is Mr. Fan Xudong. The enterprises created by Fan have a strong influence in North China. Wu personally created Tianchu Monosodium Glutamate, Tianli Nitrous Gas, Tianyuan Electrochemistry, and Tiansheng Ceramics in Shanghai. These four factories are the crystallization of his efforts and are also national industries related to national defense. Mr. Wu is not only meticulous in his career, but also diligent in learning and health. He is honest and respectful in his conduct and is a model for the public. What kind of person is his wife, Ms. Dai Yi? Perhaps few people outside know. Well, let me tell you, she is a worker who combines knowledge and action and is also worthy of being called a model for women. The following is a quick sketch of my interview.

When I walked into the Tianchu General Management Office, I saw the staff extremely busy. On one side, there were three female employees talking to male and female workers. Mr. Wu invited me into the reception room. I explained my purpose, first asking about his residence. He pointed to the fourth floor of the factory building. Then I asked about his wife, and he quickly went to the next room to ask her to come over. He said with a smile, "I don't have a mansion. That room is our bedroom. She works in the factory all year round." It turned out that one of the female employees I saw was Mrs. Wu, who is the factory affairs director of Tianchu. She has been working on time every day since its establishment in May 1923, without ever being absent. She is in charge of worker management, product review, and work allocation. She said, "Now there are more people in the factory, and with the division of labor and cooperation, things are easier to handle. In the early days, we both took on everything, big and small." Ah! This wife is truly remarkable. She wears homespun clothes, does not use any makeup, and is strong and full of energy. "Madam, who has been in charge of the household affairs for more than ten years while you have been working hard in the factory?" I asked her this question first. "My family is extremely simple. That bedroom has nothing but beds, chairs, tables, and benches. We both work and eat in the factory all day long, and only go there to rest at night. We hire an old nanny to take care of me. She has been hired for more than 20 years. I only have one son, who graduated from Shanghai University this summer and will soon go to the United States to study. Without the burden of children, I can fulfill my abilities. To be honest, I am not good at socializing. In addition to work, I have seventy or eighty female work companions. They are meticulous in their work and go to the club in their spare time to play various games. The factory treats them very well, and they are also very content. We are close to each other, like a family. Among them, there are many young girls who are ambitious. They studied at the literacy school for two months and are still determined to learn. I took it upon myself to guide them in subjects such as Chinese language, mathematics, and common sense. I answer all questions. I feel that all industrial and commercial organizations, if they can be united from top to bottom and treat each other with sincerity, will never have unexpected disputes. After all, people have sympathy. Do you think that's right?" This is a very moving passage from Mrs. Wu.

"What is your attitude towards social welfare undertakings?" "Because factory affairs are more complicated, I don't often hear about external matters. In recent years, I have joined the Shanghai Women's Progressive Association, and I am honored to serve as a member of the standing committee. Whenever there are women who have unhappy families and get divorced and have nowhere to go, I maintain their lives. Every year, I use my own funds to nurture poor children, and there are more than a dozen of them. Five years ago, Mr. Wu established the Qinghan Education Fund Association, and I was the first to agree. Every year, we recruit twelve people and send them to domestic universities, providing them with all expenses. Two classes have already graduated. We provide them with all expenses, each requiring seven or eight hundred gold per year. In five years, we have spent six or seven thousand yuan. They are very able to endure hardship and are very promising in the future. Last year, Mr. Wu proposed to purchase two Tianchu airplanes and donate them to the government. He initially sought my consent. I said that the country is in trouble, everyone should have the heart to save the country, and this move is enough to call on the people to build national defense. I extremely agree." Mrs. Wu also talked about her usual attitude towards Mr. Wu, and she said it very pertinently. She said, "People who serve the society inevitably encounter unsatisfactory things. Someone like him, who is always harmonious, sometimes gets stimulated. I am a woman, and I have no long-term strategy other than to use words to comfort him. Everything can be done by one's own efforts, and everything can be overcome. Mr. Wu has one advantage: he only works hard for his career and does not care about the trivial matters at home. Even when he goes out on a long trip, I advise him not to worry about anything, anyway, household affairs are easy to handle. We only have one day off a week, and we usually have very little entertainment. Only during the New Year holidays do we have the opportunity to travel and enjoy a few days of leisurely happiness."

I feel that what they have done is truly for the welfare of the people and to restore the vitality of the society and the country. This kind of great spirit is worthy of being imitated by everyone. Nowadays, human desires are rampant and social customs are declining. Therefore, I do not hesitate to use words to introduce outstanding people, just to persuade everyone to be good people and do good deeds. If I overpraise others, then I am afraid that I will be subverting right and wrong!

Shen Bao Local Supplement

Has Abyssinia Fallen? 201

— Shi Ji

Italy has long publicly declared the annexation of Abyssinia. The Abyssinian Emperor's speech at the League of Nations has also become a historical record. Even this stubborn emperor seems to have become discouraged. According to Reuters, he arrived in London from Geneva, "looking dejected." — The so-called sanctions against Italy will also be announced to be lifted from the 15th.

However, has Abyssinia really fallen from now on?

No, absolutely not! Whether the Abyssinian Emperor is "looking dejected" or not, we cannot determine the future of Abyssinia based on this. The League of Nations has long been defiled by the great powers. This is an obvious fact. Weak countries cannot rely on the League of Nations to survive. This lesson does not need to be learned by Abyssinia. We Chinese have long suffered enough. If the Abyssinian Emperor is truly "looking dejected" because of the disappointment given to him by the League of Nations this time, then it is only the Abyssinian Emperor's personal matter. The people of Abyssinia, in their recently published declaration, said clearly: "All the people of Abyssinia, except those in Addis Ababa, who are under the oppression of the Italian army and cannot move, have unanimously decided that as soon as the rainy season arrives, they will continue to resist the enemy, even if they are empty-handed, they will fight to the end to defend their country's independence and drive the brutal enemy out of their sacred land. Otherwise, anyone who is worthy of the name of Abyssinian will fight until not a single person is left..."

From this, we know how the people of Abyssinia are determined to have no enemy but themselves. If they do not "drive the brutal enemy" "out of the sacred land," then the people of Abyssinia will "fight until not a single person is left." This is not only said grandly in the declaration, but the facts also tell us: "...In the past two months, armed and elite 'bandits' (?) fiercely resisted the Italian army. One night in the Abyssinian capital, many Italian soldiers were found with their throats cut...The Italian army is mostly stationed in large cities due to difficult transportation to the interior and dare not go far. Several hundred Italian troops in Asba-Sassa-Fari were surrounded by thousands of armed Abyssinians. The Italian authorities said that they cannot be rescued." (Reuters, Cairo, 6th)

From the above telegram, it clearly tells us: Abyssinia has not been destroyed by Italy! Although Mussolini is elated and says that he has annexed Abyssinia, the reality is not entirely so.

Now, the rainy season is about to begin. After reading the above declaration, what will we think? However, we know that if we really only have "empty hands," it is very difficult to "fight to the end" (the past battles, as well as waiting for the rainy season to begin so that the Italian army's planes cannot operate, are not the best illustrations?). Therefore, we express extraordinary sympathy and hope for their "appeal to the British people in the name of a dying nation to provide assistance in raising 5 million to 6 million pounds of public bonds for the purpose of resisting the enemy in the parts of the country not occupied by the Italian army." We hope that just people all over the world can lend a hand to this "dying nation." They said, "We do not currently ask other countries to send troops to help us, nor do we want soldiers from other countries to lightly shed a drop of blood to save our country's independence. What we ask for is only a small amount of money to purchase arms. Once we have arms, the rest of the work can be done by Abyssinian soldiers themselves"! To such earnest and tragic words, to such a pitiful and brave nation, are we really going to watch them "fight until not a single person is left"? Is world justice really always in the hands of the great powers?

China's fate today is not above Abyssinia. Abyssinia has prepared for a "unanimous decision" to fight to the end. What about us?

The Abyssinian people's declaration excites us and also makes us confident: We are confident that Abyssinia will not perish! In the lessons of blood, we see what the inevitable fate of small and weak nations is?

What we have to do is: How to "defend our country's independence!"

Seaside 202

— Lao Xin

Walking out of the east gate of Baoshan County, the scene before us seemed to suddenly open up. An unusual, pleasant, and fresh feeling shot straight into our minds like an arrow. All of a sudden, a fresh and soft sea breeze floated over, driving away the dark shadows. The mind, which had been blocked by the coal smoke of the city, was also gradually blown open by this beautiful and magnificent nature, blown open.

My childhood temperament broke out again, and I ran wildly and ecstatically onto this river embankment. An indescribable joy tore me away from everything and gave me to Mother Nature. Even if this was a great sin, I might be willing to accept the unjustness.

A roar came from the bottom of my heart—Mother Nature! Why don't you surge your waves, wash away all the ugliness in this world, and submerge this unreasonable old society? May you respond to the heart's voice of these millions of righteous people, who urgently need your encouragement, who are willing to stir up the storm of this era!

The heroic posture of the waves crashing on the shore is very moving. The waves struggling with the boulders, being squeezed and bursting out in all directions, are so spirited. The sound of battle when rushing to fight—the "crashing, crashing, crashing—sand!" shouting, is like the last roar of millions of oppressed people: majestic and breaking the enemy's courage.

This is Wusongkou, where the Huangpu River flows into the sea. In front of us is a vast expanse of white, and the horizon is nowhere to be seen. At the end of our vision, a line of gray stripes separates the two seas—the ever-changing sea of clouds and the surging waves. In this crude picture, there are also a few elegant and noble sails embellishing it. Sometimes, when looking at traditional Chinese paintings, I always feel that adding a few sails is pretentious and deliberately separates the painting from reality. This concept has now been denied by myself, but I am not saying that the sails in traditional Chinese paintings are appropriate. On the contrary, I am just admiring the courage of these small creatures struggling with nature. Combined with the surging waves, it is not contradictory, but harmonious, mutually reflecting the beauty of "strength."

It is a cloudy day. No sun. No storm. However, I don't know by what force, the crests of the waves, like millions of arms linked together, stretched out their giant palms, towering high, and proudly expressing their anger!—The anger suppressed for who knows how many years, the anger erupting from the hearts of millions of people!

"Be braver, young people!

Relying on the strength of millions of us,

Tear apart the old,

Relying on the strength of millions of us,

Create the new!........."

Encouraged by Mother Nature, I sang madly like this.

When my travel companion told me that the friend who was seeing us off had left us and returned to Baoshan City, I woke up a little. At this time, I realized that I was still in this chaotic society. However, what made me happy was that I remembered: In this long journey of endurance, I am no longer lonely. I have not only found travel companions, but there are not just one, but millions. So, clasping the hand of this friend, we resolutely embarked on this small journey of ours with a brisk pace, with joy and delight.

We both promised each other: We would walk along the seaside until we reached Wusong Town, and then change ships. This small walk would take about fifty or sixty minutes, or perhaps even more. During this time, we would be accompanied by this roaring sea until we were forced to leave it by the ruthless environment.

These times are very precious. We cherish them. We don't want to waste them even a little. We don't even want to spend them in meaningless conversations. Therefore, during these times, we entrusted our whole body and mind to our mother—this magnificent and surging sea. That is to say, even the beating of our hearts follows the crashing of the waves.

My love for the seaside is not a rare sight in my youth. I have had intermittent seaside life for nearly two years; living by the seaside, from childhood, I don't know how many days. I don't know how many stories I have about the seaside alone. I can't remember them all at this time. I would like to have an opportunity to tell the beautiful and ordinary seaside stories to my heart's content. However, time is sometimes very cruel, and before I could swallow my fill of this sea and sky, I was forced to board the small train to the metropolis again. It dragged me step by step away from the realm I loved and threw me back into the crucible of life.

I miss this seaside journey. I yearn for that second time when we are completely free.

Random Notes from Yangshi 203

— Ai Tu

The Dragon Boat Tragedy

The Dragon Boat Festival has arrived again, and the southerners living in the semi-tropics are enthusiastically starting dragon boat races. Two days ago, my brother asked me to go home, but I didn't go after all. I said, "What's the point? The countryside is just annoying!" Actually, I had already promised Annie. I was going to watch the dragon boat races with her in the provincial capital. She would jump up and down like a child. She grew up in Guangzhou and knows everything better than I do. So, I didn't want to leave the provincial capital, waiting like a hungry cat for the arrival of that strange dragon boat comedy.

In the morning, the sun was fiercely burning the roads of Shameen, and the doors of all the shops along the road were tightly closed. Everyone was celebrating the festival, the day to commemorate Qu Yuan! However, this has become a superstitious custom for people. Few people know what the meaning of the Dragon Boat Festival is!

Running out onto the road, I saw dragon boats on land making loud noises. A long dragon, its colorful colors swaying in the white sunlight, with more than ten people riding inside its belly, strutting around so arrogantly - this is a dragon! But, seeing them everywhere made me feel dizzy.

Annie and I went to Shameen, that paradise-like place - that's the imperialists' concession! That day, it seemed to be under martial law, refusing entry to many people who didn't look like upper-class people. However, we finally ran in, and on that shaded coastline, like guests in a paradise, we leaned back in our chairs, breathing in the fresh sea breeze, watching the small boats floating on the turbulent White Swan Lake.

"Here they come! Look, those three dragon boats are desperately rushing over!"

Annie pouted her little mouth, pointing to the dragon boats flying over the white waves. They were racing fast, the sound of gongs and drums, shouts, like the world was coming undone, looking like three mad dragons roaring. My heart was also pounded urgently.

Suddenly, we saw an electric boat, neither too big nor too small, flying in from afar into White Swan Lake. Its crazed appearance was enough to prove that it was full of "powerful people," perhaps people who came to watch the dragon boat comedy. However, this electric boat rushed towards the dragon boats on this side recklessly, a sight that made the heart tremble. It was truly terrifying:

"Alas! Lai! Look, the waves of White Swan Lake are very turbulent!"

Annie's eyes were clearly filled with worry and fear.

I held my breath. I completely forgot why I was standing so still on the beach, watching. I was even more afraid to hear that terrible wail:

"Hey! Avoid! Avoid!"

This was a roar from the dragon boat, but it was too late. The electric boat had approached the small dragon boat. Both sides went from anxiety to roar, but the electric boat was ultimately arrogant, or it didn't avoid and rushed over. The people on the dragon boat couldn't suppress their anger and raised their paddles, yet they couldn't disregard the small boat swaying in the huge waves. In the midst of the shouting, we heard and saw gunshots fired from the electric boat. The people on the dragon boat closest to the electric boat fell into the water. In the raging waves, a dragon boat overturned, and more than fifty people were submerged in the water of White Swan Lake.

The electric boat still sailed safely into the city, but our eyes were watching that tragedy, and our eyes became blurred.

"Ah! Such a barbaric world!"

Annie's eyes became moist. She looked at me, and then at the blue sky. The sun in the sky was shining brightly on the surface of White Swan Lake, the white waves still floating without any change, the sea breeze still coolly blowing on us. However, my face drooped, and I didn't dare to look at the waves anymore.

The next morning, we saw this news in the newspaper:

"An electric boat carrying the Huo family members went to the province to watch the dragon boat races. Due to a head-on collision with a dragon boat, the dragon boat overturned, killing more than thirty people!"

After reading it, my heart became even more uneasy and waves arose, "Why can't the newspaper say a few more words! Why is it so calm!"

Annie covered my mouth with her hand, meaning there was no need to say it. I sighed and closed my eyes!
